ترجمة الإمام الصاوي
نصيب عند الإمام الصاوي، ولكن ما نزلوا من قلبه كمنزلة شيخه ومربيه أوحد زمانه العلامة البحر الشيخ أحمد الدردير الله وعنهم أجمعين . في رحاب الشيخ الدردير
العلامة الدردير كان نجم الهداية في سماء إمامنا الصاوي رحمهما الله، وكانت عُلقة كلِّ منهما بصاحبه تجاوز حدود المألوف، قال العلامة المؤرخ الجبرتي في ترجمة الإمام الدردير لله : (الإمام العالم العلامة، أوحد وقته في الفنون العقلية والنقلية، شيخ أهل الإسلام وبركة الأنام أبو البركات أحمد بن محمد بن أحمد بن أبي حامد العدوي المالكي الأزهري الخلوتي الشهير بالدردير، ولد ببني عدي كما أخبر عن نفسه سنة (١١٢٧هـ) وحفظ القرآن وجوده ، وحُبِّب إليه طلب العلم، فورد الجامع الأزهر وحضر العلماء وسمع الأوَّليَّ عن الشيخ محمد الدقري بشرطه، والحديث على كل من الشيخ أحمد الصباغ وشمس الدين الحفني وبه تخرّج في طريق القوم، وتفقه على الشيخ علي الصعيدي ولازمه في جلّ درسه حتى
دروس
أكبر
أنجب وتلقن الذكر وطريق الخلوتية من الشيخ الحفني، وصار من خلفائه، وأفتى في حياة شيوخه، مع كمال الصيانة والزهد والعفة والديانة، وحضر بعض دروس الشيخين الملوي والجوهري وغيرهما، ولكن جل اعتماده وانتسابه على الشيخين الحفني ،والصعيدي وكان سليم الباطن
مهذب النفس ، كريم الأخلاق) (۱) .
(۱) عجائب الآثار (۳۳/۲) .

ومؤلفات العلامة الدردير لها مكانة رفيعة بين كتب المتأخرين عند السادة المالكية، وخريدته» و «صلواته» و «تحفته» لا تغيب عن مكتبة طلبة العلم المجدِّين، فمتى وكيف عرف الصاوي دليل قلبه إلى ربِّه؟
في السنة التي وفد فيها الفتى الصاوي إلى القاهرة قاصداً الأزهر (۱۱۸۷هـ) ، وبعد ستة أشهر أقامها يومها جذبته الطلعة الحرة البهية ذات الأنوار الربانية للشيخ الدردير لأن يكون منتظماً في عقد الولاية، ووقع نظر الأحمدين على بعضهما، وحيرة الحياء والوجل تغلي في فؤاد الفتى، لتتجلى نظرة منكسرة راجية تخالطها نظرة أبوية حانية متوقدة تلألاً شعشاعُها تجولُ فى صفحات وجه الوصية الربانية الوافدة، ويبايع الشيخ الدردير ولده الروحي الصاوي، ويرتضيه ليثاً في طريق السادة الخلوتية، طريق العلم والعمل والولاية والأدب مع الله تعالى ومع رسوله المصطفى عليه صلوات الله وسلاماته .
ولك أن تعلم أن الشيخ الدردير قام فنسج الصاوي نسيجاً جديداً لا تبليه الأيام، فأخذ عنه المعقول والمنقول وهو يومها إمام مصر كلها فيهما، وتفقه على يديه حتى بلغ الأمر أن إذا رأى الشيخ الدردير خط الصاوي
على فتوى ما . . سارع وختم عليها ؛ لعلمه بتدينه وتحقيقه العلمي هذا ملازم لمجالس الشيخ وأوراده، لا يني ولا يتأوَّل، حتى
والصاوي مع
كان له في قلب الشيخ المقام الأول.
(۱) مناقب الصاوي ( ص ٦٤) .
Translation of Imam al-Sawi: He had a share with Imam al-Sawi, but they (i.e., his shaykhs) held a place in his heart like that of his shaykh and educator, the unique one of his time, the ocean of knowledge, Shaykh Ahmad al-Dardir—may Allah be pleased with him and with them all. In the precincts of Shaykh al-Dardir. Al-‛Allāmah al-Dardir was the star of guidance in the sky of our Imam al-Sawi—may Allah have mercy on them both. The bond between each of them and his companion exceeded the usual limits. Al-‛Allāmah al-Mu’arrikh al-Jabartī said in his biography of Imam al-Dardir—may Allah be pleased with him: “The Imam, the scholar, the unique one of his time in the rational and transmitted sciences, the shaykh of the people of Islam and the blessing of mankind, Abu al-Barakāt Aḥmad ibn Muḥammad ibn Aḥmad ibn Abī Ḥāmid al-‛Adawī al-Mālikī al-Azharī al-Khalwatī, known as al-Dardir. He was born in Banī ‛Adī, as he himself reported, in the year 1127 AH. He memorized the Qur’an and recited it with tajwīd, and love for seeking knowledge was instilled in him. He came to al-Azhar Mosque and attended the scholars. He heard al-Awwalī from Shaykh Muḥammad al-Duqarī with its conditions, and hadith from both Shaykh Aḥmad al-Ṣabbāgh and Shams al-Dīn al-Ḥifnī—and under the latter he graduated in the path of the people (i.e., the Sufis). He studied fiqh under Shaykh ‛Alī al-Ṣa‛īdī and accompanied him in most of his lessons until he became proficient and produced outstanding students. He received the dhikr and the way of the Khalwatiyya from Shaykh al-Ḥifnī and became one of his successors. He issued fatwas during the lifetime of his shaykhs, with complete integrity, asceticism, chastity, and piety. He attended some lessons of the two shaykhs al-Mallawī and al-Jawharī and others, but his main reliance and affiliation was on the two shaykhs al-Ḥifnī and al-Ṣa‛īdī. He was pure-hearted, refined in soul, and noble in character.” (1) (1) ‛Ajā’ib al-Āthār (2/33). And the works of al-‛Allāmah al-Dardir hold a lofty status among the later books of the Malikī masters. His al-Kharīdah, his Ṣalawāt, and his Tuḥfah are never absent from the library of diligent students. So when and how did al-Sawi come to know the guide of his heart to his Lord? In the year when the young al-Sawi arrived in Cairo heading for al-Azhar (1187 AH), after six months he had spent there, his noble, radiant countenance, possessing divine lights, attracted him to Shaykh al-Dardir in order to be included in the circle of sainthood. The two Aḥmads’ eyes fell upon each other, and the confusion of shyness and fear seethed in the young man’s heart, so that a humble, hopeful look appeared, mingled with a compassionate, paternal, glowing gaze whose brilliance moved across the pages of the arriving divine bequest. And Shaykh al-Dardir pledged allegiance to his spiritual son al-Sawi, and accepted him as a lion in the path of the Khalwatī masters—the path of knowledge, action, sainthood, and good manners with Allah Almighty and with His Messenger the Chosen One—upon him be the prayers and peace of Allah. And you should know that Shaykh al-Dardir took charge and wove al-Sawi into a new fabric that time does not wear out. So he learned from him the rational and transmitted sciences—while he was at that time the leading imam of all Egypt in both—and he studied fiqh under his guidance until it reached the point that when Shaykh al-Dardir saw al-Sawi’s handwriting on some fatwa, he would hasten to endorse it, knowing his piety and scholarly investigation. Al-Sawi was constant in attending the shaykh’s gatherings and regularly performing his litanies, never slackening or finding excuses. And al-Sawi held the foremost place in the shaykh’s heart. (1) (1) Manāqib al-Ṣāwī (p. 64).
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This is a biographical passage from the book's introduction, describing the relationship between Imam al-Sawi and his shaykh, Ahmad al-Dardir. It begins by stating that despite al-Sawi having many teachers, none held the place in his heart that al-Dardir did. The author then provides a detailed biography of al-Dardir, quoting the historian al-Jabarti. Al-Jabarti's biography lists al-Dardir's full name and lineage, his birth year (1127 AH), his early education—memorizing the Quran, studying with various shaykhs at al-Azhar—and his specialization in both rational and transmitted sciences. It highlights his teachers: al-Duqari for al-Awwali, al-Sabbagh and al-Hifni for hadith, and al-Sa'idi for fiqh. He also received the Khalwati order from al-Hifni and became a successor. The passage notes his virtues: issuing fatwas while his shaykhs were alive, his asceticism, chastity, and piety. After the quote, the author remarks on the high status of al-Dardir's works among Malikis. The narrative then shifts to how al-Sawi met al-Dardir: al-Sawi came to Cairo in 1187 AH, and after six months, he was drawn to al-Dardir. Their meeting is described poetically: eyes met, and al-Dardir accepted al-Sawi as a spiritual son, initiating him into the Khalwati path. The passage concludes by noting that al-Dardir taught al-Sawi both rational and transmitted sciences, so much so that al-Dardir would immediately endorse al-Sawi's fatwas due to his trust in his piety and scholarship. Al-Sawi was diligent in attending al-Dardir's gatherings and litanies, and he held the highest place in al-Dardir's heart.

Key Terms
الشيخ الصاوي
الشيخ الدردير
الخلوتية
الجامع الأزهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the bond was merely scholarly, but the passage emphasizes a deep spiritual father-son relationship.
Correction: The passage describes al-Dardir as pledging allegiance to 'his spiritual son' and speaks of the gaze and the initiation into the Khalwati path, indicating a spiritual bond beyond academics.

Checkpoint
In which year did al-Sawi first arrive in Cairo to seek knowledge at al-Azhar?
A) 1127 AH
B) 1187 AH
C) 1175 AH
D) 1200 AH

Key Takeaway
The meeting between al-Sawi and al-Dardir was a transformative spiritual encounter that shaped al-Sawi's entire scholarly and spiritual life.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look back on your life, can you identify a person whom Allah guided you to at a critical moment? Have you been as attentive and constant in learning from them as al-Sawi was with al-Dardir? What excuse do you have for not seeking their knowledge with the same diligence?
?
The passage describes a gaze of humility and hope from al-Sawi. In your interactions with those who have more knowledge or spirituality, do you carry that same humble, hopeful look, or do you rely on your own opinion? What would it cost you to adopt that posture starting today?
?
Al-Sawi held the foremost place in the shaykh's heart because of his diligence. What is one relationship you have neglected—with a teacher, parent, or spiritual guide—that needs renewal? Will you take a concrete step to reconnect this week?

Life of Imam al-Sawi
beginner

Al-Sawi's Arrival and Bond with al-Dardir
Narrates al-Sawi's arrival in Cairo and his initiation with Sheikh al-Dardir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of al-Sawi's relationship with his teacher al-Dardir, both spiritually and academically, and how this bond formed the foundation of his scholarly career.

Core Idea
The spiritual and scholarly bond between al-Sawi and al-Dardir was the foundation of al-Sawi's formation.

This biographical passage recounts the first meeting between the young Ahmad al-Sawi and his future teacher, the eminent scholar Ahmad al-Dardir, in Cairo. It describes a profound spiritual attraction that led to a lifelong teacher-student relationship, combining both the Sufi path of the Khalwati order and rigorous academic training in the Islamic sciences. Through this story, we glimpse the ideal of Islamic learning where spiritual mentorship and intellectual mastery go hand in hand.

Guided Path
1
Set the scene: arrival in Cairo
Read the opening line carefully. Note the year (1187 AH) and al-Sawi's purpose: heading to al-Azhar. After six months, something significant happens.
The year is important for historical context.
2
Observe the spiritual attraction
Al-Sawi is drawn by al-Dardir's radiant countenance. Notice the language: 'free, beautiful countenance with divine lights' – this is not just a physical description but a spiritual one.
Look for words like 'أنوار ربانية' (divine lights).
3
Understand the exchange of glances
The two 'Ahmads' eyes meet. The author describes a mix of shyness and awe in al-Sawi's heart, contrasted with a compassionate, paternal gaze from al-Dardir.
This parallel sets up the teacher-student dynamic.
4
Recognize the initiation into the Khalwati Path
Al-Dardir accepts al-Sawi as a spiritual son and initiates him into the Khalwati order. Note the qualities of this path: knowledge, action, sainthood, and etiquette.
The phrase 'ليثاً في طريق السادة الخلوتية' – a lion in the path – denotes strength and commitment.
5
Appreciate the academic training and trust
Al-Dardir taught al-Sawi both rational and transmitted sciences. Al-Sawi's competence grew so much that al-Dardir would immediately endorse his fatwas, trusting his piety and scholarship.
This shows the depth of their intellectual relationship.

في السنة التي وفد فيها الفتى الصاوي إلى القاهرة قاصداً الأزهر (۱۱۸۷هـ) ، وبعد ستة أشهر أقامها يومها جذبته الطلعة الحرة البهية ذات الأنوار الربانية للشيخ الدردير لأن يكون منتظماً في عقد الولاية، ووقع نظر الأحمدين على بعضهما، وحيرة الحياء والوجل تغلي في فؤاد الفتى، لتتجلى نظرة منكسرة راجية تخالطها نظرة أبوية حانية متوقدة تلألاً شعشاعُها تجولُ فى صفحات وجه الوصية الربانية الوافدة، ويبايع الشيخ الدردير ولده الروحي الصاوي، ويرتضيه ليثاً في طريق السادة الخلوتية، طريق العلم والعمل والولاية والأدب مع الله تعالى ومع رسوله المصطفى عليه صلوات الله وسلاماته . ولك أن تعلم أن الشيخ الدردير قام فنسج الصاوي نسيجاً جديداً لا تبليه الأيام، فأخذ عنه المعقول والمنقول وهو يومها إمام مصر كلها فيهما، وتفقه على يديه حتى بلغ الأمر أن إذا رأى الشيخ الدردير خط الصاوي على فتوى ما . . سارع وختم عليها ؛ لعلمه بتدينه وتحقيقه العلمي هذا ملازم لمجالس الشيخ وأوراده، لا يني ولا يتأوَّل، حتى كان له في قلب الشيخ المقام الأول.
In the year when the young al-Sawi came to Cairo heading for al-Azhar (1187 AH), and after six months he had stayed there, he was drawn by the free, beautiful countenance with divine lights of Sheikh al-Dardir to be organized in the knot of sainthood. The two ‘Ahmads’ eyes fell upon each other, and the confusion of shyness and awe boiled in the youth's heart, so that a broken, hopeful glance appeared mixed with a compassionate, paternal gaze, blazing, its radiance shimmering, roaming over the pages of the incoming divine testament. And Sheikh al-Dardir pledged allegiance to his spiritual son al-Sawi, and accepted him as a lion in the path of the al-Khalwatiyya masters, the path of knowledge, action, sainthood, and etiquette with God Almighty and with His Chosen Messenger, upon him be the prayers and peace of God. And you should know that Sheikh al-Dardir stood up and wove for al-Sawi a new fabric that days do not wear out. He took from him the rational and transmitted sciences while he was at that time the imam of all Egypt in both. And he studied jurisprudence under him until the matter reached that when Sheikh al-Dardir saw al-Sawi's handwriting on some legal opinion, he would hasten and stamp it because of his knowledge of his piety and scholarly verification. This was constant in the assemblies of the Sheikh and his litanies, not slackening nor seeking excuse, until he had the foremost place in the Sheikh's heart.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a biographical narration describing how Ahmad al-Sawi first met his teacher, Ahmad al-Dardir, upon arriving in Cairo in 1187 AH. It portrays a spiritual attraction: al-Sawi was drawn by al-Dardir's radiant appearance after six months in Cairo. The two exchanged looks filled with modesty and awe from the student and paternal care from the teacher. Al-Dardir accepted him as a spiritual son and initiated him into the Khalwati order. The author then explains that al-Dardir remolded al-Sawi, teaching him both rational ('aqli) and transmitted (naqli) sciences, in which al-Dardir was the leading authority in Egypt. Al-Sawi became so proficient that al-Dardir would immediately endorse any fatwa al-Sawi wrote, trusting his piety and scholarly rigor. Al-Sawi was constant in attending al-Dardir's sessions and litanies until he gained the highest rank in his teacher's heart.

Key Terms
الصاوي
الدردير
الأزهر
الخلوتية

Key Takeaway
The meeting of al-Sawi and al-Dardir exemplifies the ideal of Islamic scholarship where spiritual initiation and academic excellence are inseparable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own pursuit of knowledge, do you have a teacher who sees you with a compassionate, paternal gaze? If not, what is holding you back from seeking such a bond?
?
Al-Sawi dedicated himself so completely to his sheikh that his teacher trusted his fatwas instantly. Is there any relationship in your life that demands such total trust and dedication? How would that transform your learning?
?
The passage says al-Dardir 'wove for al-Sawi a new fabric that days do not wear out.' What kind of spiritual fabric are you weaving for yourself? Will it endure the trials of life and death?

Al-Sawi's Reverence: A Lesson from a Cold Ear
Describes al-Sawi's extreme respect and a lesson from a cold ear.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Sawi's extreme reverence for his teacher led to a transformative moment of spiritual accountability.

Core Idea
A cold ear taught al-Sawi the cost of spiritual laziness.

This short anecdote from al-Sawi's biography reveals the depth of his respect for his teacher, al-Dardir. It shows how a minor gesture – a touch on a cold ear – became a powerful lesson in accountability. The story illustrates the principle that true reverence transforms one's spiritual discipline.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the story. Let the narrative flow before analyzing.
Notice the extreme behavior described.
2
Understand the reverence
Al-Sawi would not sleep while his teacher was awake, and if he slept, he slept under his feet. Consider the level of adab (respect) this shows.
3
Focus on the ear incident
Al-Dardir touched al-Sawi's ear and said 'Your ear is cold!' – a subtle reprimand for missing the litany. Reflect on how al-Sawi understood the hint immediately.
The cold ear indicates he had not risen for night prayer.
4
Reflect on the outcome
Al-Sawi felt intense shame, sweated, and resolved to never miss a litany again. If he did, he would stay up all night to compensate. Consider how shame can be a positive motivator in spiritual growth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبلغ من تعظيم الإمام الصاوي لشيخه الدردير ما تتحيَّرُ فيه العقول، فكان لا يذوق نوماً وشيخه مستيقظ، فإذا نام نام تحت رجليه، واستيقظ قبله، ولا سيما بعدما أخذ الدردير بأذنه يوماً نام فيه عن ورده وقال: أذنك باردة! قال الصاوي: (ففهمت إشارته، وتصببت عرقاً من شدة الحياء، ولزمت الهمة والاجتهاد في أخذ الأوراد، فما فاته بعد ذلك ورد للشيخ إلا وكفّره بإحياء ليلة كاملة.
The veneration of Imam al-Sawi for his Sheikh al-Dardir reached a degree that bewilders minds. He would not taste sleep while his Sheikh was awake, and if he slept, he slept under his feet and woke up before him, especially after al-Dardir took his ear one day when he had slept through his litany and said: 'Your ear is cold!' Al-Sawi said: 'I understood his hint, and I poured with sweat from intense shyness, and I adhered to determination and diligence in performing the litanies, so thereafter no litany of the Sheikh passed him by except that he expiated it by reviving an entire night.'
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is an anecdote illustrating al-Sawi's extraordinary reverence for his teacher. It states that his veneration reached mind-boggling levels: he would not sleep while his teacher was awake, and if he slept, he would sleep at his teacher's feet and wake before him. The specific incident: one day al-Dardir noticed al-Sawi had missed his litany (wird) and touched his ear, saying 'Your ear is cold!' (indicating he had not risen for the night prayer). Al-Sawi immediately felt intense shame, sweat pouring, and he resolved to never miss a litany again. If he ever did, he would compensate by staying awake the entire night in worship. This shows the deep impact of the teacher's subtle reprimand.

Key Terms
الورد
الأوراد
الأذن

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) He laughed it off

Key Takeaway
True reverence for one's teacher manifests in turning even a gentle reprimand into a catalyst for spiritual growth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When someone gently hints at a fault of yours, do you become defensive or do you, like al-Sawi, pour with sweat from shame and change? What subtle reprimands have you ignored this week?
?
Al-Sawi's veneration was so great that he could not sleep while his teacher was awake. Is there anyone in your life—parent, teacher, or spiritual guide—toward whom you feel such reverence? If not, what pride stands in the way of cultivating that respect?
?
If you knew that missing one spiritual practice would require you to stay awake all night to expiate it, would you still neglect it? Which wird have you been lazy about, and what are you willing to sacrifice to never miss it again?

Al-Dardir's Defense of al-Sawi Against Jealousy
Narrates a jealous attempt to turn al-Dardir against al-Sawi and its failure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Dardir's unwavering support for al-Sawi was demonstrated in response to jealousy, and the impact on a jealous peer.

Core Idea
True scholars recognize merit and are not swayed by envy.

This lesson recounts a biographical incident highlighting the virtue of recognizing true worth. Despite attempts to turn him against al-Sawi, al-Dardir's response was firm and revealed his high regard. The story also shows the effect on a jealous colleague, Muhammad 'Abada, who witnessed al-Sawi's special status.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation to grasp the flow of events.
Notice the key phrases and the sequence of the story.
2
Identify the key characters
List the main figures: al-Dardir, al-Sawi, the slanderers (الوشاة), and Sheikh Muhammad ‘Abada.
Consider their relationships: al-Dardir as teacher, al-Sawi as student, ‘Abada as a peer and former teacher of al-Sawi.
3
Analyze al-Dardir's response
Focus on al-Dardir's statement: 'My son Ahmad has no equal, whether he comes or does not come.' Reflect on what this reveals about his opinion of al-Sawi.
The phrase 'لا نظير له' (has no equal) is emphatic.
4
Reflect on 'Abada's reaction
Examine ‘Abada's words: he wished to strip off his own knowledge and fame to have al-Sawi's rank with al-Dardir, and his remark about the dhikr filling him with light.
This shows both envy and admiration, and highlights al-Sawi's spiritual station.

وقد حاول بعض الوشاة ممن أكلت الغيرةُ قلبَهُ تغيير قلب الشيخ الدردير في حق الصاوي، فنعته بالتفريط والغياب عن مجلس الذكر، فقال العلم الدردير: (ولدي أحمد لا نظير له أتى أو لم يأتِ)، حتى بلغ من الشيخ محمد عبادة -وهو من أقران الشيخ الدردير في الأزهر وابن بلدته، ومن جملة أشياخ الصاوي كما سبق أن جعل الصاوي وسيلته للدخول لقلب الشيخ الدردير ، ثم بعدها كان يقول : (أود أن أسلب العلم والشهرة وتكون منزلتي عند الشيخ الدردير كمنزلتك يا صاوي!)، وكان قد شاهد يوماً كيف أخذ الصاوي عن الدردير ورداً خاصاً، فقال: (لقد امتلأ قلبي وجسدي نوراً من سماعي الذكر في أذنه، فكيف بمن أدخل الذكر إلى قلبه ؟ ! ) .
And some slanderers whose hearts were eaten by jealousy tried to change Sheikh al-Dardir's heart regarding al-Sawi, accusing him of negligence and absence from the assembly of dhikr. So the scholar al-Dardir said: 'My son Ahmad has no equal, whether he comes or does not come.' This reached Sheikh Muhammad ‘Abada – who was one of al-Dardir's peers at al-Azhar and his fellow townsman, and among al-Sawi's teachers, as previously mentioned; he had made al-Sawi his means to enter al-Dardir's heart, and then after that he used to say: 'I wish I could strip off knowledge and fame and have my rank with Sheikh al-Dardir be like your rank, O Sawī!' And one day he had witnessed how al-Sawi received a special litany from al-Dardir, so he said: 'My heart and body were filled with light from my hearing the dhikr in his ear, so what about the one who brought the dhikr into his heart?'
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage relates an incident of jealousy. Some people, consumed by envy, tried to turn al-Dardir against al-Sawi by accusing him of being careless and missing the dhikr gatherings. Al-Dardir's response was firm: 'My son Ahmad has no equal, whether he attends or not.' The story then focuses on Sheikh Muhammad ‘Abada, a contemporary of al-Dardir and a former teacher of al-Sawi. He had initially used al-Sawi to gain closeness to al-Dardir. Later, 'Abada expressed a wish to trade all his own knowledge and fame for al-Sawi's rank with al-Dardir. He witnessed al-Sawi receiving a special litany from al-Dardir and remarked that just hearing the dhikr in al-Sawi's ear filled him with light, so how much more must it affect al-Sawi, who internalized it.

الغيرة

محمد عبادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Jealousy and slander can successfully turn a true scholar against his student.
Correction: Al-Dardir's response shows that a true scholar is not swayed by jealousy; he recognizes merit regardless of external accusations.

Checkpoint
What did al-Dardir say when slanderers accused al-Sawi of negligence?
A) 'He is expelled from my assembly'
B) 'My son Ahmad has no equal, whether he comes or not'
C) 'I will investigate the matter'
D) 'He must apologize'

Key Takeaway
Al-Dardir's unwavering defense of al-Sawi demonstrates that true mentorship is immune to jealousy and slander.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Al-Dardir's defense of al-Sawi was immediate and absolute. Is there a person in your life whose worth you would defend unconditionally, even when they are absent? If not, what does that reveal about your own attachments?
?
Muhammad ‘Abada wished to trade his knowledge and fame for a higher rank with al-Dardir. What worldly status or accomplishment are you holding onto that might be a barrier to true spiritual closeness with Allah or His saints? Will you release it?

Al-Sawi's Reverence and the Ear-Pulling Incident
Narrates al-Sawi's extreme reverence and the ear-pulling incident.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the depth of respect and self-discipline in traditional Islamic learning through the story of Imam al-Sawi and his teacher al-Dardir.

Core Idea
True reverence transforms mistakes into opportunities for greater devotion.

This account from the biography of Imam al-Sawi illustrates a profound teacher-student bond. It shows how a simple corrective gesture – a pulled ear and a few words – sparked a lifetime of intensified worship and discipline. As you read, consider the role of shame (haya') in motivating positive change.

Guided Path
1
Read the anecdote
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Let the story unfold without analyzing it immediately.
Pay attention to the intense language: 'متحير فيه العقول' (minds are bewildered).
2
Identify the key elements
Notice the teacher's action (ear-pulling and the comment), the student's reaction (sweating from shame, understanding the hint), and the resolution (intensified litanies and expiation).
3
Reflect on the lesson
Ask yourself: What does this story teach about the purpose of haya' and the teacher-student relationship? How did al-Sawi's response demonstrate true reverence?
The story is not about blind obedience but about sincere personal growth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة الإمام الصاوي
وبلغ من تعظيم الإمام الصاوي لشيخه الدردير ما تتحيَّرُ فيه العقول، فكان لا يذوق نوماً وشيخه مستيقظ، فإذا نام نام تحت رجليه، واستيقظ قبله، ولا سيما بعدما أخذ الدردير بأذنه يوماً نام فيه عن ورده وقال: أذنك باردة! قال الصاوي: (ففهمت إشارته، وتصببت عرقاً من شدة الحياء، ولزمت الهمة والاجتهاد في أخذ الأوراد، فما فاته بعد ذلك ورد للشيخ إلا وكفّره بإحياء ليلة كاملة)
Translation of Imam al-Sawi. The veneration of Imam al-Sawi for his teacher al-Dardir reached a level that minds are bewildered by. He would not taste sleep while his teacher was awake; when he slept, he slept at his feet, and woke before him. Especially after al-Dardir one day took his ear (when al-Sawi had slept through his litany) and said: 'Your ear is cold!' Al-Sawi said: 'I understood his hint, and sweat poured from me from the intensity of shame, and I resolved to be diligent and earnest in performing the litanies; after that, whenever he missed a litany of the shaykh, he would expiate it by reviving an entire night.'
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a biographical anecdote illustrating al-Sawi's extraordinary reverence for his teacher al-Dardir. It begins by stating that his veneration reached an unimaginable degree. Then it provides two concrete examples: first, his constant alertness—he would not sleep while his teacher was awake, and when he did sleep, he would lie at his teacher's feet and wake before him. The second and more specific example is the ear-pulling incident. One day, al-Sawi missed his wird (daily litany) because he slept, so al-Dardir pulled his ear and said 'Your ear is cold!' as a reprimand. Al-Sawi immediately understood the implicit rebuke, felt intense shame (sweating profusely), and resolved to be diligent. From then on, if he ever missed a wird, he would expiate it by staying awake the entire night in worship. This shows the deep respect and strict self-discipline that characterized the teacher-student relationship in traditional Islamic learning.

Key Terms
الورد
الحياء
الكفارة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think al-Sawi's reverence was exaggerated or blind obedience.
Correction: The text shows it was a sincere, disciplined response that led to increased worship, not just sycophancy.

Checkpoint
What did al-Sawi do whenever he missed a litany (wird) of his teacher after the ear-pulling incident?
A) He would apologize.
B) He would expiate it by reviving an entire night.
C) He would skip it.
D) He would ask for forgiveness.

Key Takeaway
True reverence for a teacher manifests in constant awareness and a commitment to self-improvement, even after a gentle reprimand.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When a teacher or parent corrects you, do you feel the same depth of shame and resolve that al-Sawi felt, or do you make excuses? What one change can you make today to respond better to correction?
?
Think of a religious practice you have been neglecting. What would it take for you to treat it with the same seriousness as al-Sawi treated his wird, so that missing it drives you to immediate expiation?
?
Are you truly aware of the sacrifices your teachers make for you? Do you prioritize their comfort and your own spiritual discipline, or do you take their efforts for granted? What is one concrete action you can take this week to show greater reverence for them?

Al-Dardir's Unwavering Defense of al-Sawi
Anecdote about al-Dardir defending al-Sawi from slanderers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Dardir's response to slander reveals the high spiritual rank of al-Sawi and the transmission of blessing (baraka) in traditional Islamic learning.

Core Idea
Al-Dardir's defense shows that true rank is spiritual, not based on outward attendance.

This passage recounts a moment when jealous slanderers tried to turn the great scholar al-Dardir against his student al-Sawi. Al-Dardir's reply not only dismisses the accusation but elevates al-Sawi's status. The anecdote also illustrates how peer scholars recognized al-Sawi's special blessing.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the literal translation to understand the narrative.
This passage is a short biographical story, not dense theology.
2
Identify the slander and al-Dardir's response
Notice the accusation: al-Sawi was described as 'negligent and absent from the gathering of dhikr'. Then see al-Dardir's strong rebuttal: 'My son Ahmad has no equal, whether he comes or does not come.'
Al-Dardir's response implies that al-Sawi's spiritual state is independent of physical presence.
3
Reflect on Shaykh Muhammad 'Abada's reaction
Muhammad 'Abada, a peer of al-Dardir, expressed a wish to have al-Sawi's standing and was filled with light just by hearing the wird transmission. This shows how even senior scholars recognized al-Sawi's elevated rank.
'Abada was also one of al-Sawi's teachers, making his acknowledgment even more significant.
4
Consider the concept of spiritual transmission
The transmission of the wird (litany) from al-Dardir to al-Sawi and the effect of hearing it on 'Abada illustrates the baraka (blessing) passed through the teacher-student chain.
The light (nur) mentioned is a sign of divine blessing and knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد حاول بعض الوشاة ممن أكلت الغيرةُ قلبَهُ تغيير قلب الشيخ الدردير في حق الصاوي، فنعته بالتفريط والغياب عن مجلس الذكر، فقال العلم الدردير: (ولدي أحمد لا نظير له أتى أو لم يأتِ)، حتى بلغ من الشيخ محمد عبادة -وهو من أقران الشيخ الدردير في الأزهر وابن بلدته، ومن جملة أشياخ الصاوي كما سبق أن جعل الصاوي وسيلته للدخول لقلب الشيخ الدردير، ثم بعدها كان يقول : (أود أن أسلب العلم والشهرة وتكون منزلتي عند الشيخ الدردير كمنزلتك يا صاوي!)، وكان قد شاهد يوماً كيف أخذ الصاوي عن الدردير ورداً خاصاً، فقال: (لقد امتلأ قلبي وجسدي نوراً من سماعي الذكر في أذنه، فكيف بمن أدخل الذكر إلى قلبه ؟ !)
And indeed, some slanderers whose hearts were consumed by jealousy attempted to alter the heart of Shaykh al-Dardir regarding al-Sawi. They described him as negligent and absent from the gathering of dhikr. So the scholar al-Dardir said: 'My son Ahmad has no equal, whether he comes or does not come.' This reached such a degree that Shaykh Muhammad 'Abada—who was one of al-Dardir's peers at al-Azhar and from his hometown, and one of al-Sawi's teachers as previously mentioned, and whom al-Sawi had made his means to enter al-Dardir's heart—afterwards used to say: 'I wish I could strip away knowledge and fame, and have the same standing with Shaykh al-Dardir as you, O Sawi!' And he had witnessed one day how al-Sawi took a specific litany (wird) from al-Dardir, so he said: 'My heart and body became filled with light from my hearing the dhikr in his ear; how then about the one who inserted the dhikr into his heart?!'
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is another biographical anecdote demonstrating al-Dardir's unwavering confidence in al-Sawi and the high esteem in which he was held even by his peers. It begins by describing a slanderer (wushah) motivated by jealousy trying to turn al-Dardir against al-Sawi, accusing him of negligence and absence from the dhikr gathering. Al-Dardir's response is emphatic: 'My son Ahmad has no equal, whether he comes or not.' This implies that al-Sawi's spiritual state is so elevated that his physical presence is not the measure. The narrative then mentions Shaykh Muhammad 'Abada, a peer of al-Dardir and also one of al-Sawi's teachers. This shaykh had used al-Sawi as a means to gain closeness to al-Dardir, which shows al-Sawi's intercessory role. After seeing al-Sawi receive a special wird directly from al-Dardir, 'Abada expressed his wish to exchange his own knowledge and fame for al-Sawi's status with al-Dardir. He also remarked that merely hearing the dhikr transmitted to al-Sawi's ear filled him with light, so how much more must the recipient himself be filled? This highlights the perceived spiritual transmission and the high rank of al-Sawi.

الغيرة (jealousy)

النور (light)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Dardir's statement was merely a polite defense, not indicating actual superiority.
Correction: Al-Dardir said 'لا نظير له' (no equal to him), which is an absolute statement of unmatched status, not just politeness.

Checkpoint

C) 'Al-Sawi is negligent.'
D) 'Al-Dardir is unfair.'

Key Takeaway
Al-Dardir's defense of al-Sawi reveals that spiritual rank and baraka are not dependent on outward attendance but are recognized by those of true insight.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your standing with your teacher or in your community depended solely on your outward attendance, would you be content? Or do you, like al-Sawi, have a connection that transcends presence? Examine your own heart: are you more concerned with being seen or with the reality of your bond with Allah and His awliya?
?
Imagine you witnessed a disciple receiving a special litany from a master and felt the light fill you just from hearing it. Would you be moved to humility and gratitude, or would jealousy consume you, like the slanderers? When you see others blessed with spiritual gifts, do you celebrate their rank or secretly wish to take their place? What can you strip away from your own ego today to be more like Muhammad 'Abada in his honest admiration?
?
Al-Dardir declared al-Sawi has no equal 'whether he comes or does not come.' Are there people in your life whose spiritual value you judge by their attendance alone? How can you train yourself to see beyond the outward to the inner reality, so that you recognize the true saints among you, even when they are hidden? Commit today to asking Allah for the insight to see people as they truly are.

Al-Sawi's Devotion to His Teacher al-Dardir
Anecdote of al-Sawi's constant companionship until al-Dardir's death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the depth of the teacher-student bond in traditional Islamic learning through the example of al-Sawi and al-Dardir.

Core Idea
Loyalty in seeking knowledge is shown through constant companionship and trust.

This lesson presents a touching story from the life of al-Sawi and his shaykh al-Dardir. It illustrates the ideal relationship between a student and his teacher, where service and care are paired with deep mutual respect. As you read, consider how this reflects the spirit of traditional Islamic education.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the emotional tone and key phrases.
Pay attention to the words 'ملازمة' (constant companionship) and 'لا أقطع' (I will not entrust).
2
Analyze the interaction
Consider why al-Dardir asked for al-Sawi and why he felt he was late. The bystanders' response reveals al-Sawi's constant presence.
Al-Dardir's longing ('اشتاق') shows his high regard for al-Sawi.
3
Reflect on the final statement
Al-Dardir says he will not entrust his funeral to anyone else. What does this imply about al-Sawi's status?
This indicates complete trust and recognition of al-Sawi's worth.
4
Connect to broader themes
Think about how this story exemplifies the adab (etiquette) of seeking knowledge and the teacher-student relationship in Islam.
It also shows the importance of service (khidma) in traditional learning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بقي الصاوي ملازماً لشيخه الدردير إلى آخر لحظة من حياته، وكان الشيخ الدردير أيام مرضه يسأل عنه ويقول: أين ولدي أحمد؟ فيقولون: هو أسفل الدار، فأمر بمجيئه، فصعد إليه، فقال له الشيخ : لم تأخرت يا ولدي؟ ثلاثة أيام وأنا مشتاق إليك، فقال الحاضرون : إنه لم يخرج من المنزل منذ أن حصل لك المرض، فقال الشيخ : إن مت لا أقطع بأحد غير ولدي أحمد .
Al-Sawi remained constantly accompanying his shaykh al-Dardir until the last moment of his life. During his illness, Shaykh al-Dardir would ask about him and say: 'Where is my son Ahmad?' They would say: 'He is at the bottom of the house.' So he ordered him to come, and he ascended to him. The shaykh said to him: 'Why were you late, my son? For three days I have been longing for you.' The attendees said: 'He has not left the house since you became ill.' The shaykh said: 'If I die, I will not entrust (my funeral) to anyone other than my son Ahmad.'
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage illustrates the deep attachment between al-Sawi and his teacher, especially in the teacher's final illness. It begins by stating that al-Sawi remained in constant attendance until the very end. During al-Dardir's illness, he would ask for al-Sawi, and when told he was downstairs, he summoned him. When al-Sawi arrived, al-Dardir chided him gently, saying he had been missing him for three days. The bystanders explained that al-Sawi had not left the house at all, implying that the perceived delay was not due to neglect but perhaps the teacher's heightened longing. Then al-Dardir makes a striking statement: if he dies, he will entrust his funeral rites (often interpreted as leading the funeral prayer) to no one but al-Sawi. This shows complete trust and a clear indication of al-Sawi's spiritual and scholarly rank in the eyes of his teacher.

Key Terms
ملازمة (constant companionship)
مرض (illness)
الاشتياق (longing)
القطع (entrusting)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think al-Dardir was unaware of al-Sawi's presence, but the attendees knew he was always at home; it was the teacher's intense longing that made him feel delayed.
Correction: Al-Dardir's question 'Why were you late?' reflects his longing, not al-Sawi's absence. The attendees confirm al-Sawi's constant presence.

Checkpoint

A) 'I will appoint a different scholar.'
B) 'I will not entrust it to anyone other than my son Ahmad.'
C) 'It should be simple.'
D) 'I do not want a funeral.'

Key Takeaway
The story demonstrates the deep trust and love between a teacher and student, where constant companionship and service earn the teacher's ultimate endorsement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are in the presence of your teacher, are you fully present, or is your mind elsewhere? What would it take for you to be like al-Sawi, who never left his shaykh's house during his illness?
?
If your teacher were on their deathbed, would they entrust their final affairs to you? What does your current level of service and love for them say about your relationship? What can you change today to deepen that trust?
?
Do you long for your teachers as al-Dardir longed for al-Sawi? When you are away from them, do you feel that same ache? How can you cultivate that love and connection in your heart?

Life of Imam al-Sawi

Al-Sawi's Spiritual Discipline
Narrates al-Sawi's spiritual exercises and extreme self-discipline.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of al-Sawi's spiritual struggles (mujahadat) and how he disciplined his soul under the guidance of his shaykh.

Core Idea
Spiritual discipline begins with gentleness and culminates in mastery over the soul's cravings.

This passage from al-Sawi's biography reveals the inner dimension of traditional Islamic education: the cultivation of the soul through ascetic practices (mujahadat). It begins with an encounter between al-Sawi and his shaykh, al-Dardir, who shows special care for him while emphasizing the difficulty of the path. The narrative then illustrates al-Sawi's extreme self-discipline, including how he responded when his soul desired sweet food. This lesson invites you to reflect on the balance between being harsh and gentle with oneself in the spiritual journey.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage silently
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the story sink in without immediate analysis.
Notice the emotional tone: weeping disciples, a gentle shaykh, and a determined seeker.
2
Observe the teacher's interaction
How does al-Dardir treat the group versus al-Sawi? What does this tell you about al-Sawi's spiritual state?
Al-Dardir's leniency indicates al-Sawi already possessed a high degree of discipline.
3
Examine the discipline of the nafs
Trace al-Sawi's response to his soul's craving for sweets. Why did he not just say no? What did he do instead?
He left food and drink entirely for three nights—a radical response.
4
Reflect on the test of the dates
When the dates arrived unasked, al-Sawi initially took them but didn't eat until an inner prompting told him it was permissible. What principle is at work?
This shows reliance on spiritual insight and gratitude without excess.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مجاهداته في طريق القوم :
يوماً لقن الشيخ الدردير جملة من مريديه ورداً خاصاً، وكان بينهم العلامة السيد خير الدين الغزي فقال لهم : الطريق صعب، وهذا أول قدم يضعه المريد فيها، فكونوا على حالة طيبة والزموا الآداب، ولما وصل الصاوي . . قال له يا ولدي ؛ ارفق بنفسك؛ إن لبدنك عليك حقاً، فقام الجماعةُ من عند الشيخ باكين على أنفسهم ؛ بتشديده عليهم وتخفيفه على الصاوي
فقد كان الإمام لا يأكلُ إلا لقيمات قليلة ويلازم الجوع من غير صوم فضلاً عن الصوم، ودخل الخلوة بأمر شيخه، فبقي ثلاث ليال يأكل قليلاً من الأرز، فاشتهت نفسه طعاماً حلواً فأدَّبها بأن ترك الطعام والشراب ثلاث ليال، حتى صار يسمع نفسَهُ حالَ الذكر تقول : يا مغيثُ ؛ أغثنا، فإذا برجل يطرق الباب ومعه تمر حسن، فأخذه وأغلق الباب، ولم يأكل، حتى عرض في قلبه : شيء أتاك بلا طلب، فكله فصار يأكل في اليوم ثلاث تمرات لا يزيد عليها !
His spiritual struggles in the path of the folk (Sufis): One day, Shaykh al-Dardir taught a group of his disciples a special litany (wird), among them the notable Sayyid Khayr al-Din al-Ghazzi. He said to them: 'The path is difficult, and this is the first step the disciple places in it, so be in a good state and adhere to the etiquette.' When al-Sawi arrived… he said to him: 'O my son, be gentle with yourself; your body has a right upon you.' The group then left the shaykh weeping upon themselves because of his severity towards them and leniency towards al-Sawi. Indeed, the Imam would only eat a few morsels and would persist in hunger even when not fasting, let alone when fasting. He entered seclusion (khalwa) by order of his shaykh, and stayed three nights eating little rice. Then his soul desired a sweet food, so he disciplined it by leaving food and drink for three nights, until during dhikr he could hear his own soul saying: 'O Supporter, support us!' Then a man knocked at the door with good dates. He took them and closed the door, but did not eat, until it occurred to his heart: 'Something came to you without asking, so eat it.' So he began eating three dates a day, not more.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a description of al-Sawi's spiritual struggles (mujahadat) on the Sufi path. It begins with an incident where al-Dardir gives a special wird to a group of disciples, including the scholar Khayr al-Din al-Ghazzi. Al-Dardir emphasizes the difficulty of the path and the need for proper conduct. When al-Sawi arrives, al-Dardir tells him to be gentle with himself, noting that the body has rights, showing al-Dardir's special care for al-Sawi's well-being. The other disciples weep because al-Dardir was severe with them but lenient with al-Sawi, highlighting al-Sawi's unique status. The next part details al-Sawi's personal asceticism. He ate very little, constantly hungry. He entered spiritual seclusion (khalwa) and ate only a little rice for three nights. When his soul craved sweet food, he disciplined it by abstaining from all food and drink for three more nights. His spiritual state became so intense that during dhikr he could hear his inner self crying out for divine help (ya mughith). Then a man came with high-quality dates. Al-Sawi took them but initially did not eat, until he felt an inner prompting that since it came without asking, it was permissible, so he began to eat only three dates per day. This demonstrates his extreme self-control and reliance on spiritual signs.

Key Terms
المجاهدات (spiritual struggles)
الخلوة (seclusion)
الورد (wird)
النفس (soul/self)
الذكر (dhikr)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Sawi's asceticism was physically harmful.
Correction: It was a disciplined spiritual training under the guidance of his shaykh, with periods of abstention and reliance on divine signs, not self-harm.

Checkpoint
How did al-Sawi discipline his soul when it desired sweet food?
A) He ate sweets sparingly.
B) He left food and drink for three nights.
C) He increased his dhikr.
D) He asked his shaykh for permission.

Key Takeaway
Al-Sawi's story illustrates that true spiritual discipline involves both external practice and internal response to divine provision, always under the guidance of the shaykh and with attention to the soul's rights.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When your own soul (nafs) craves something that goes against your spiritual goals, what method do you use to discipline it—do you give in, or do you, like al-Sawi, take a drastic step? What would it take for you to hear your own soul crying out for divine help rather than momentary satisfaction?
?
Al-Sawi limited himself to three dates after receiving them unasked. When you receive an unexpected blessing, do you consume it thoughtfully or do you rush to indulge? How can you practice both gratitude and restraint in your next moment of receiving?
?
The shaykh told al-Sawi to be gentle with himself, yet al-Sawi was extremely hard on his own cravings. In your own spiritual training, are you more like the other disciples who needed severity, or like al-Sawi who needed a check from harshness? Reflect on whether you have been avoiding necessary discipline or overburdening yourself, and set one concrete adjustment for this week.

Al-Sawi's Spiritual Struggles and Ascetic Discipline
Narrative of al-Sawi's spiritual training and ascetic discipline

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the role of disciplined self-denial and sheikh-guided spiritual training in the Sufi path as exemplified by Imam al-Sawi.

Core Idea
Spiritual growth requires balance between divine guidance, self-discipline, and moderation.

Imam al-Sawi's biography provides a vivid example of the Sufi principle of mujahada (spiritual struggle). The passage relates two key episodes: his sheikh's warning about the difficulty of the path, and his own severe ascetic practices during seclusion. As you read, notice how al-Sawi's actions are not merely self-imposed but are a response to spiritual insight and his sheikh's direction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage once
Read the Arabic passage and its translation without analyzing. Let the story unfold and capture the emotional and spiritual tone.
Pay attention to the contrast between the other disciples and al-Sawi.
2
Identify the two main parts
The passage has two clear parts: the group lesson with al-Dardir (lines 1-5), and al-Sawi's personal ascetic practices including his seclusion (lines 5-end). Notice the different attitudes.
3
Analyze al-Sawi's actions
List the specific actions al-Sawi took: eating little, fasting, seclusion, disciplining his soul when it desired sweets, and later restricting himself to three dates.
These actions are progressive and purposeful.
4
Reflect on the guiding principle
Al-Sawi's asceticism is not random; it is guided by his sheikh's advice ('be gentle with yourself') and by inner spiritual insights (the soul crying for help, the dates arriving without asking).
This shows the balance between effort and divine grace.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مجاهداته في طريق القوم : يوماً لقن الشيخ الدردير جملة من مريديه ورداً خاصاً، وكان بينهم العلامة السيد خير الدين الغزي فقال لهم : الطريق صعب، وهذا أول قدم يضعه المريد فيها، فكونوا على حالة طيبة والزموا الآداب، ولما وصل الصاوي . . قال له يا ولدي ؛ ارفق بنفسك؛ إن لبدنك عليك حقاً، فقام الجماعةُ من عند الشيخ باكين على أنفسهم ؛ بتشديده عليهم وتخفيفه على الصاوي (١) فقد كان الإمام لا يأكلُ إلا لقيمات قليلة ويلازم الجوع من غير صوم فضلاً عن الصوم، ودخل الخلوة بأمر شيخه، فبقي ثلاث ليال يأكل قليلاً من الأرز، فاشتهت نفسه طعاماً حلواً فأدَّبها بأن ترك الطعام والشراب ثلاث ليال، حتى صار يسمع نفسَهُ حالَ الذكر تقول : يا مغيثُ ؛ أغثنا، فإذا برجل يطرق الباب ومعه تمر حسن، فأخذه وأغلق الباب، ولم يأكل، حتى عرض في قلبه : شيء أتاك بلا طلب، فكله فصار يأكل في اليوم ثلاث تمرات لا يزيد عليها !
His struggles in the path of the people: One day Sheikh al-Dardir taught a group of his disciples a special litany, and among them was the scholar Sayyid Khayr al-Din al-Ghazzi, and he said to them: The path is difficult, and this is the first step the disciple places in it, so be in a good state and adhere to the etiquettes. And when al-Sawi arrived... he said to him: O my son, be gentle with yourself; indeed your body has a right over you. So the group got up from the sheikh crying over themselves because of his severity upon them and his leniency upon al-Sawi. (1) The Imam used to eat only small mouthfuls and was constantly hungry without fasting, let alone fasting. He entered seclusion by his sheikh's order, and he remained three nights eating little rice. Then his soul desired sweet food, so he disciplined it by leaving food and drink for three nights, until he began to hear his soul during remembrance saying: O Helper, help us! Then a man knocked at the door with good dates. He took them and closed the door, but did not eat, until it occurred to his heart: Something came to you without asking, so eat it. So he began to eat three dates a day, not more!
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of Imam al-Sawi's spiritual struggles (mujahadat). It begins with a story illustrating the discipline of the Sufi path: Sheikh al-Dardir, al-Sawi's teacher, gave a special litany to his disciples, warning them that the path is difficult and that this is their first step. When al-Sawi arrived, al-Dardir told him to be gentle with himself because his body has rights over him. The other disciples wept because al-Dardir was strict with them but lenient with al-Sawi, highlighting al-Sawi's advanced state. Then the passage describes al-Sawi's asceticism: he ate very little, constantly hungry even without formal fasting, and his fasting was even more intense. He entered seclusion (khalwa) by his sheikh's order. For three nights he ate only a little rice. When his soul desired sweets, he disciplined it by abstaining from all food and drink for three nights. During dhikr, he heard his own soul crying out for divine help. A man then brought him good dates. He took them but initially did not eat, until he reflected that the food came without his seeking, so he should eat. Thereafter he limited himself to three dates a day. This demonstrates the Sufi principles of self-discipline, reliance on God, and moderation even in permissible things.

خلوة
ذكر

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Sawi's asceticism was purely self-imposed and extreme without guidance.
Correction: The text shows his practices were done under his sheikh's order (بأمر شيخه) and in response to spiritual insights (the soul's cry, the unasked-for dates).

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
True spiritual discipline combines rigorous self-denial with humble submission to divine will and sheikhly guidance, as seen in al-Sawi's restricted eating and response to the unasked-for dates.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you craved something for your soul (like sweetness or ease) and instead of indulging immediately, you disciplined yourself by waiting or abstaining? What did that reveal about your spiritual strength?
?
Al-Sawi's soul cried out 'O Helper, help us' during his struggle. In your own life, when you face deep spiritual dryness or difficulty, do you recognize that cry within you, or do you turn to distractions? What would it take for you to sit in silence and let your soul speak?
?
The dates came to al-Sawi without his seeking. When blessings (a new opportunity, a friendship, a moment of peace) come to you unbidden, do you accept them with gratitude and restraint, or do you immediately want more? How does your response reflect your trust in Allah's timing and provision?

Al-Sawi's Multiple Sufi Affiliations and Scholarly Praise
Lists al-Sawi's Sufi orders and gives scholarly praise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Imam al-Sawi was initiated into multiple Sufi orders and highly praised by scholars for his guidance and character.

Core Idea
Al-Sawi synthesized multiple Sufi paths and was celebrated as a unique spiritual guide.

This passage completes al-Sawi's biography by detailing his spiritual training across several Sufi orders and presenting testimonies of his impact. You will see how his teachers spanned different lineages, and how his students and contemporaries extolled his virtues.

Guided Path

The quotes emphasize guidance, mercy, and his unique status.

This counters the misconception that he followed only one path.

وقد تأدَّب الإمام بجملة من طرق السادة الصوفية؛ فقد تلقى الطريقة الخلوتية عن شيخه الدردير وعن الشيخ عبد المتعال الخراشي، والطريقة الشاذلية عن الإمام عبد الوهاب العفيفي، والخراشي أيضاً، والطريقة القادرية عن السيد أعرابي البيروتي، وكذا الطريقة الدمرداشية عنه، بل وأخذ جملة الطرق الصوفية عن الإمام محمد الأمير الكبير الله . أخلاقه وثناء العلماء عليه : ألسنةُ الخلق أقلام الحق ، قال السيد أحمد الششتي تلميذ الإمام الصاوي في الكتاب السالف الذكر مناقب الصاوي»: اشتغل بالإرشاد إلى طريق الرشاد، وأنقذ الله به مهج العباد من الحسد والبغي والعناد، فعم نفعه الحاضر والباد. التشديد يربي أتباعه ثم إن أستاذي - له وعنَّا به - شرع يدعو الناس إلى الله بحاله ،وقاله وحاله مع عباد الله العطف والرأفة وعدم بالألحاظ في كل الألحاظ، ويدلهم على المقام الأعلى من أول قدم، حتى فاح شذا عطره في الأكوان، وانتشر سره في جميع الوديان). وقال العلامة محمد بن ظافر المدني الأزهري المالكي في كتابه اليواقيت الثمينة في أعيان مذهب عالم «المدينة» (٦٤/١): (العلامة المحقق، والجهبذ الفهامة الحبر المدقق وحيد الزمان، وفريد العصر ، والآن قدوة السالكين ومربي المريدين شيخ الوقت والطريقة العابر من المجاز إلى الحقيقة لم أقف له على ترجمة، وأخذ الله عن سيدي أحمد الدردير، وسيدي محمد الأمير الكبير، ومن في طبقتهما إلى أن
And the Imam was disciplined by a number of the paths of the Sufi masters: he received the Khalwati order from his sheikh al-Dardir and from Sheikh Abd al-Muta'al al-Kharashi; and the Shadhili order from Imam Abd al-Wahhab al-Afifi, and also from al-Kharashi; and the Qadiri order from Sayyid Arabi al-Beiruti; and likewise the Damardashiyya order from him; indeed he took all the Sufi orders from Imam Muhammad al-Amir al-Kabir. His character and the praise of scholars upon him: The tongues of creation are the pens of truth. Sayyid Ahmad al-Shashti, the student of Imam al-Sawi, said in the aforementioned book 'Manaqib al-Sawi': He occupied himself with guidance to the path of right guidance, and God saved through him the lives of servants from envy, transgression, and stubbornness, so his benefit encompassed the settled and the desert. Severity raises his followers. Then my teacher—may God benefit us through him—began to call people to God by his state and his speech, and his state with God's servants was kindness and mercy and lack of scrutiny in every glance, and he directed them to the highest station from the first step, until the fragrance of his scent spread in the worlds, and his secret spread in all valleys. And the scholar Muhammad ibn Zahir al-Madani al-Azhari al-Maliki said in his book 'al-Yawaqit al-Thamina fi A'yan Madhhab 'Alam al-Madina' (1/64): The accomplished scholar, the ocean, the great understanding, the erudite investigator, the unique of the time, the singular of the age and moment, the exemplar of the wayfarers and the trainer of the disciples, the sheikh of the time and the path, the one who passes from the metaphorical to the real—I have not found a biography for him. And he took from my master Ahmad al-Dardir and my master Muhammad al-Amir al-Kabir and those of their class until...
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage completes the biography of Imam al-Sawi by listing his affiliations with various Sufi orders and presenting praise from scholars. First, it enumerates the orders he received: the Khalwatiyya from his primary teacher al-Dardir and also from al-Kharashi; the Shadhiliyya from al-Afifi and again from al-Kharashi; the Qadiriyya from al-Beiruti; the Damardashiyya from the same; and he even took all Sufi orders from Muhammad al-Amir al-Kabir. This shows his comprehensive training and integration of multiple spiritual lineages. Next, it describes his character and the praise of scholars. It quotes a student, Ahmad al-Shashti, who wrote a book on al-Sawi's virtues, stating that al-Sawi dedicated himself to guiding others and that God saved people from vices through him. It also quotes al-Madani, who praises al-Sawi with superlatives, calling him the unique scholar and exemplar of the path. The passage ends abruptly with mention that he studied under al-Dardir and al-Amir, likely continuing the chain of transmission.

Three Scholarly Testimonies to Imam al-Sawi
Three scholars praise Imam al-Sawi's character and spiritual lineage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how three respected scholars testified to Imam al-Sawi's spiritual rank, scholarly stature, and place in the Khalwati order.

Core Idea
Three scholarly voices unite to affirm Imam al-Sawi's sainthood and learning.

This lesson presents excerpts from three esteemed scholars who praised Imam al-Sawi. Their testimonies establish his significance as a scholar, guide, and link in the Khalwati order. Reading their words helps us see how later generations honored him.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the structure

2
Examine each testimony's focus
For each scholar, identify what they emphasized: al-Shashti on al-Sawi's teaching and compassion, al-Madani on his erudition and date of death, al-Nabhani on his place in the Khalwati chain.
3
Reflect on the overall purpose
Ask yourself: why collect these testimonies? How do they collectively establish al-Sawi's authority?
This connects to the common misconception about al-Sawi being the founder of the order.

ألسنةُ الخلق أقلام الحق ، قال السيد أحمد الششتي تلميذ الإمام الصاوي في الكتاب السالف الذكر مناقب الصاوي»: اشتغل بالإرشاد إلى طريق الرشاد، وأنقذ الله به مهج العباد من الحسد والبغي والعناد، فعم نفعه الحاضر والباد. التشديد يربي أتباعه ثم إن أستاذي - له وعنَّا به - شرع يدعو الناس إلى الله بحاله ،وقاله وحاله مع عباد الله العطف والرأفة وعدم بالألحاظ في كل الألحاظ، ويدلهم على المقام الأعلى من أول قدم، حتى فاح شذا عطره في الأكوان، وانتشر سره في جميع الوديان). وقال العلامة محمد بن ظافر المدني الأزهري المالكي في كتابه اليواقيت الثمينة في أعيان مذهب عالم «المدينة» (٦٤/١): (العلامة المحقق، والجهبذ الفهامة الحبر المدقق وحيد الزمان، وفريد العصر ، والأوان قدوة السالكين ومربي المريدين شيخ الوقت والطريقة العابر من المجاز إلى الحقيقة لم أقف له على ترجمة، وأخذ الله عن سيدي أحمد الدردير، وسيدي محمد الأمير الكبير، ومن في طبقتهما إلى أن قال وتوفي بالمدينة المنورة سنة إحدى وأربعين ومئتين وألف لله). وقال إمام أهل السنة في عصره العلامة يوسف النبهاني في كتابه «جامع كرامات الأولياء»: الشيخ أحمد الصاوي شيخ الطريقة الخلوتية، وأستاذها الأعظم في مصر، بعد شيخه الشيخ أحمد الدردير أستاذها الأعظم في مصر، بعد شيخه الشيخ محمد الحفني أستاذها الأعظم في مصر، بعد شيخه السيد مصطفى البكري أستاذها الأعظم ومجددها الأكرم، ولكل منهم كرامات كثيرة، وأعظمها معرفتهم برب العالمين، وتسليكهم المريدين الصادقين، وكلُّهم من أكابر العلماء والأولياء الله العارفين، رضي عنهم أجمعين، ونفعنا ببركاتهم آمين، وعنهم انتشرت هذه الطريقة العلية في بلاد مصر والحجاز والشام والمشرق والمغرب وسائر البلاد الإسلامية.
The tongues of creation are the pens of truth. Sayyid Ahmad al-Shashti, the student of Imam al-Sawi, said in the previously mentioned book 'Manaqib al-Sawi': 'He occupied himself with guiding to the path of righteousness, and Allah saved the people's hearts through him from envy, transgression, and obstinacy, so his benefit encompassed the present and the remote. ... Then my teacher - may Allah be pleased with him and through us - began to call people to Allah by his state, his speech, and his conduct with the servants of Allah: compassion, mercy, and not [showing] scorn in any regard, and he would guide them to the highest station from the very first step, until the fragrance of his scent wafted through the worlds and his secret spread throughout all valleys.' And the scholar Muhammad bin Dhafir al-Madani al-Azhari al-Maliki said in his book 'al-Yawaqit al-Thamina' (1/64): 'The investigator scholar, the expert, the understanding, the scrutinizing scholar, the unique of time, the unparalleled of age and time, the exemplar of seekers, the educator of disciples, the shaykh of the time and the path, the one who crosses from metaphor to reality. I have not found a biography of him, and he studied with Sayyidi Ahmad al-Dardir, Sayyidi Muhammad al-Amir al-Kabir, and those of their rank until ... he said: He died in al-Madinah al-Munawwarah in the year 1241 AH.' And the Imam of Ahl al-Sunnah in his time, the scholar Yusuf al-Nabhani, said in his book 'Jami' Karamat al-Awliya': 'Shaykh Ahmad al-Sawi is the shaykh of the Khalwati order, and its greatest teacher in Egypt, after his shaykh Ahmad al-Dardir its greatest teacher in Egypt, after his shaykh Muhammad al-Hifni its greatest teacher in Egypt, after his shaykh Mustafa al-Bakri its greatest teacher and most noble renewer. And each of them has many miracles, and the greatest of them is their knowledge of the Lord of the worlds and their guidance of sincere disciples. And they are all among the greatest scholars and the gnostics, may Allah be pleased with them all, and benefit us through their blessings, amen, and through them this exalted order spread in the lands of Egypt, the Hijaz, Syria, the East, the West, and other Islamic lands.'
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage compiles three authoritative testimonies to Imam al-Sawi's stature. It begins with a proverb: 'The tongues of creation are the pens of truth.' Then it quotes his student Ahmad al-Shashti, who praises his guidance and character. Next, Muhammad bin Dhafir al-Madani excels in praise and notes his death in 1241 AH. Finally, Yusuf al-Nabhani places al-Sawi in the chain of the Khalwati order, tracing the lineage of its great teachers and emphasizing the spread of the order. The passage aims to establish al-Sawi's high rank among scholars and saints.

The Karama of Imam al-Sawi: Knowledge of the Unseen
Narration of al-Sawi's miracle predicting death and consoling disciple.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a karama (divine grace) manifested in Imam al-Sawi's knowledge of the unseen and his prophetic consolation to a disciple.

Core Idea
Saints know hidden events by Allah's permission as divine grace.

This passage presents a specific miracle (karama) of Imam Ahmad al-Sawi, as narrated by his disciple Husayn al-Jisr. It shows al-Sawi's spiritual insight into the death of a man before news arrived, and his comforting words that the disciple's father would become a 'bridge' (jisr) by Allah's permission. The story illustrates the Sufi concept of karamat and the relationship between shaykh and disciple.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
First, read the Arabic passage carefully, then read the literal translation. Pay attention to the names and the flow of the story.
The passage ends abruptly; note that the story likely continues.
2
Identify key elements
Identify: Who are the main figures? What did al-Sawi instruct? How did the disciple react? What was the glad tiding?
The pun on 'jisr' (bridge) is central.
3
Reflect on the significance
Think about why this account is considered a karama. What does it reveal about al-Sawi's spiritual state and his role as a guide?
In Sufi tradition, karamat are signs of closeness to Allah, not independent powers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن كرامات سيدي الشيخ أحمد الصاوي ما ذكره صديقي العلامة الأكمل الشيخ حسين ابن الولي الكبير العارف الشهير سيدي الشيخ محمد الجسر الطرابلسي أحد أكابر خلفاء الشيخ أحمد الصاوي المذكور، قال الشيخ حسين المذكور في كتابه نزهة «الفكر الذي ألفه في مناقب والده الشيخ محمد الجسر : وقد بلغني من كرامات سيدي الشيخ أحمد الصاوي قدس الله سره وبشاراته بوالدي أنه قبل أن يرد خبر وفاة جدي والد الشيخ إلى مصر، قال سيدنا الصاوي في حضور والدي ومحفل من إخوانه: أسمعونا الفاتحة لروح الحاج مصطفى الجسر ؛ يعني : جدي! فجعل والدي يبكي، فأخذ سيدنا الشيخُ الصاوي يعزّيه، ثم إنه جعل يضرب ظهره بيده الكريمة ويقول له : أنت جسر بإذن الله ، أنت جسر بإذن الله، ثم بعد مدة
And among the karama of my master Shaykh Ahmad al-Sawi is what was mentioned by my friend, the most complete scholar, Shaykh Husayn, son of the great saint and famous gnostic, my master Shaykh Muhammad al-Jisr al-Tarabulusi, one of the senior deputies of the aforementioned Shaykh Ahmad al-Sawi. The mentioned Shaykh Husayn said in his book 'Nuzhat al-Fikr' which he authored on the virtues of his father, Shaykh Muhammad al-Jisr: 'It reached me from the karama of my master Shaykh Ahmad al-Sawi (may Allah sanctify his secret) and his glad tidings concerning my father, that before the news of the death of my grandfather (the father of the shaykh) reached Egypt, our master al-Sawi said in the presence of my father and a gathering of his brothers: "Recite the Fatiha for the soul of al-Hajj Mustafa al-Jisr" – meaning my grandfather. So my father began to weep, and our master Shaykh al-Sawi began to console him, and then he started patting his back with his noble hand and saying to him: "You are a bridge (jisr) by the permission of Allah, you are a bridge by the permission of Allah." Then after a while...'
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage recounts a specific karama (miraculous event) attributed to Imam al-Sawi. It is reported by Husayn al-Jisr in his book about his father. The story demonstrates al-Sawi's knowledge of the unseen, as he knew that the father of Muhammad al-Jisr had died before news arrived. He then consoled Muhammad al-Jisr and gave him the glad tiding that he would become a 'bridge' (jisr) by Allah's permission. The account is typical of Sufi hagiography, illustrating the shaykh's spiritual insight and his role in guiding disciples.

The Spiritual Lineage of Imam al-Sawi
Biographical note with chain of transmission and praise

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of Imam al-Sawi's place in the Khalwatiyya order as described by Yusuf al-Nabhani.

Core Idea
A saint's knowledge of Allah is his greatest miracle.

This passage from the commentary on al-Kharida records the death of Imam al-Sawi and then quotes Yusuf al-Nabhani, a renowned Sunni scholar, praising al-Sawi's spiritual lineage. It illustrates how traditional scholars valued both scholarly and spiritual authority. Let's read it carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Notice the style of the biographical entry.
The passage begins with a simple death date and then transitions into a praise quotation.
2
Identify the chain of shaykhs
Find the names of the four shaykhs mentioned in Nabhani's description. Note how each is described as 'the greatest teacher in Egypt'.
The chain goes: al-Bakri -> al-Hifni -> al-Dardir -> al-Sawi.
3
Reflect on the greatest miracle
Nabhani lists many miracles but singles out one as the greatest. Identify it and think about why knowledge of Allah is considered the highest miracle.
This connects to the core idea of the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وتوفي بالمدينة المنورة سنة إحدى وأربعين ومئتين وألف لله). وقال إمام أهل السنة في عصره العلامة يوسف النبهاني في كتابه «جامع كرامات الأولياء»: الشيخ أحمد الصاوي شيخ الطريقة الخلوتية، وأستاذها الأعظم في مصر، بعد شيخه الشيخ أحمد الدردير أستاذها الأعظم في مصر، بعد شيخه الشيخ محمد الحفني أستاذها الأعظم في مصر، بعد شيخه السيد مصطفى البكري أستاذها الأعظم ومجددها الأكرم، ولكل منهم كرامات كثيرة، وأعظمها معرفتهم برب العالمين، وتسليكهم المريدين الصادقين، وكلُّهم من أكابر العلماء والأولياء الله العارفين، رضي عنهم أجمعين، ونفعنا ببركاتهم آمين، وعنهم انتشرت هذه الطريقة العلية في بلاد مصر والحجاز والشام والمشرق والمغرب وسائر البلاد الإسلامية.
He said: And he died in Medina in the year 1141 AH). And the Imam of the Ahl al-Sunnah in his time, the scholar Yusuf al-Nabhani, said in his book 'Jami' Karamat al-Awliya': 'Shaykh Ahmad al-Sawi is the master of the Khalwatiyya order, and its greatest teacher in Egypt, after his shaykh Shaykh Ahmad al-Dardir its greatest teacher in Egypt, after his shaykh Shaykh Muhammad al-Hifni its greatest teacher in Egypt, after his shaykh Sayyid Mustafa al-Bakri its greatest teacher and most noble renewer. And each of them has many miracles, and the greatest of them is their knowledge of the Lord of the worlds, and their guiding of sincere disciples. And all of them are among the greatest scholars and the awliya' who are knowers of Allah, may Allah be pleased with them all, and benefit us through their blessings, amin. And through them this lofty order spread in the lands of Egypt, Hijaz, Syria, the East, the West, and all Islamic lands.'
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note and an authoritative praise. It first states that Imam al-Sawi died in Medina in 1141 AH. Then it quotes Yusuf al-Nabhani, a leading Sunni scholar, describing al-Sawi's position as the master (shaykh) of the Khalwatiyya order and its greatest teacher (ustadh al-a'zam) in Egypt. Nabhani then traces al-Sawi's spiritual lineage through a chain of shaykhs: al-Dardir, al-Hifni, and al-Bakri, each described as the greatest teacher and/or renewer. He emphasizes that all these shaykhs possessed many miracles (karamat), the greatest being their knowledge of Allah and their guidance of disciples. They are all among the greatest scholars and awliya'. Through them, the Khalwatiyya order spread widely. The passage concludes with a prayer for divine pleasure and blessings.

Correction: Nabhani emphasizes al-Sawi's role as the master of the Khalwatiyya order and highlights the miracles and knowledge of Allah as the greatest virtue.

Life of Imam al-Sawi

A Karama of Imam al-Sawi: Foreknowledge of a Death
Narration of a miracle where al-Sawi announced a death before news arrived.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of a saintly miracle (karama) as exemplified by Imam al-Sawi's foreknowledge of a death across a distance before any natural means could bring the news.

Core Idea
Saints can receive divine knowledge beyond natural means.

The passage presents a specific miracle of Shaykh Ahmad al-Sawi, a renowned scholar and saint. Through an eyewitness account, it demonstrates that spiritual insight can transcend physical barriers. This story also illustrates the high station of al-Sawi, who is recognized by consensus as a leading wali. As you read, notice how the narrative emphasizes the absence of natural communication, underscoring the supernatural nature of the event.

Guided Path
1
Identify the characters
Read the narrative and note the main figures: Shaykh Ahmad al-Sawi, Shaykh Husayn al-Jisr, and Shaykh Muhammad al-Jisr.
The story is transmitted through a chain of trustworthy people.
2
Observe the timing
Al-Sawi announced the death before any news could arrive from Syria, at a time when there was no telegraph or regular mail.
This emphasizes the supernatural nature of the knowledge.
3
Note the reaction and consolation
The son, Muhammad al-Jisr, wept upon hearing the request to recite Fatiha, and al-Sawi consoled him, patting his back and giving him the title 'jisr' (bridge).
This title turned out to be prophetic.
4
Reflect on the title 'jisr'
Al-Sawi repeatedly said 'You are a jisr (bridge) by the permission of Allah,' indicating a future role in connecting people to knowledge.
5
Understand the concluding statement
The author states that al-Sawi's sainthood is so well-established that it does not need many miracles; the consensus of Muslims attests to his high rank.
This reinforces the credibility of the narrated karama.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن كرامات سيدي الشيخ أحمد الصاوي ما ذكره صديقي العلامة الأكمل الشيخ حسين ابن الولي الكبير العارف الشهير سيدي الشيخ محمد الجسر الطرابلسي أحد أكابر خلفاء الشيخ أحمد الصاوي المذكور، قال الشيخ حسين المذكور في كتابه نزهة الفكر الذي ألفه في مناقب والده الشيخ محمد الجسر: وقد بلغني من كرامات سيدي الشيخ أحمد الصاوي قدس الله سره وبشاراته بوالدي أنه قبل أن يرد خبر وفاة جدي والد الشيخ إلى مصر، قال سيدنا الصاوي في حضور والدي ومحفل من إخوانه: أسمعونا الفاتحة لروح الحاج مصطفى الجسر؛ يعني جدي! فجعل والدي يبكي، فأخذ سيدنا الشيخُ الصاوي يعزّيه، ثم إنه جعل يضرب ظهره بيده الكريمة ويقول له: أنت جسر بإذن الله، أنت جسر بإذن الله، ثم بعد مدة من الزمان ورد لوالدي الخبر بوفاة والده رحمهم الله تعالى، هذا ولا يخفى أنه في ذلك الزمان لم يكن تلغراف ولا بريد منتظم بين مصر والشام. انتهى كلام الشيخ حسين الجسر حفظه الله. ومثل الشيخ أحمد الصاوي المذكور لا يحتاج للدلالة على ولايته وكثرة فضله بنقل كثير من كراماته فإنه كان بإجماع المسلمين من أكابر أئمة العلماء العاملين الهادين المهديين، وأئمة الأولياء العارفين المرشدين الكاملين، والله ينفعنا ببركاتهم آمين.
And among the miracles of my master Shaykh Ahmad al-Sawi is what my friend, the most accomplished scholar, Shaykh Husayn son of the great wali, the renowned knower, my master Shaykh Muhammad al-Jisr al-Tarabulsi — one of the great khalifas of the aforementioned Shaykh Ahmad al-Sawi — mentioned. The aforementioned Shaykh Husayn said in his book 'Nuzhat al-Fikr' which he authored on the virtues of his father Shaykh Muhammad al-Jisr: 'It has reached me from the miracles of my master Shaykh Ahmad al-Sawi — may Allah sanctify his secret — and his glad tidings regarding my father, that before the news of the death of my grandfather, the father of the shaykh, arrived in Egypt, our master al-Sawi said in the presence of my father and a gathering of his brethren: "Recite the Fatiha for the soul of al-Hajj Mustafa al-Jisr" — meaning my grandfather. So my father began to weep, and our master Shaykh al-Sawi began to console him, then he began to pat his back with his noble hand and say to him: "You are a jisr (bridge) by the permission of Allah, you are a jisr by the permission of Allah." Then after a period of time, the news of his father's death reached my father — may Allah have mercy on them. And it is not hidden that at that time there was no telegraph nor regular mail between Egypt and Syria.' End of the words of Shaykh Husayn al-Jisr, may Allah preserve him. And the likes of the aforementioned Shaykh Ahmad al-Sawi does not need to prove his sainthood and abundant virtue by transmitting many of his miracles, for he was, by the consensus of the Muslims, among the greatest imams of the righteous scholars, the guides, the guided ones, and the imams of the awliya', the knowers, the guides, the perfect ones. May Allah benefit us through their blessings, amin.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a narrative of a specific miracle (karama) of Imam al-Sawi, transmitted by Shaykh Husayn al-Jisr. The story illustrates al-Sawi's spiritual insight: before any news could have arrived from Syria (due to lack of telegraph or regular mail), al-Sawi announced the death of al-Hajj Mustafa al-Jisr and asked those present to recite al-Fatiha for his soul. He then consoled his son, Shaykh Muhammad al-Jisr, and gave him a destiny-laden title: "You are a jisr (bridge) by the permission of Allah." The narrative emphasizes the absence of natural means of communication, underscoring that this was a supernatural event. The passage then adds that al-Sawi's sainthood is so well-established that it does not require extensive documentation of miracles; the consensus of Muslims already attests to his high station as a scholar, guide, and wali.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Stories of saintly miracles are mere folklore with no basis.
Correction: The passage provides an eyewitness account and emphasizes the impossibility of natural communication, affirming the supernatural event as a genuine karama.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Al-Sawi consoled a weeping man with the words 'You are a bridge by Allah's permission.' Is there someone grieving around you right now whom you could console, not with empty words, but with a sense of divine purpose for their life?
