⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لمَّا حجَّ وقف تجاه الحجرة الشريفة النبوية وأنشد: كنتُ أُرسلها تقبل الأرض عنِّي فهي نائبتي في حالة البعد روحي وهذه نوبة الأشباح قد حضرت فامدد يمينك كي تحظى بها شفتي فخرجت اليد الشَّريفة من القبر حتّى قبّلها والنَّاس ينظرون إليها. وأخبر بوقت موته وصفته، فكان كما قال. وأراد شراء بستان، فأبى صاحبه ألا يبيعه إلَّا بقصر في الجنَّة، فارتعد وتغيَّر واصفر، ثمَّ قال: قد اشتريت منك بذلك، قال: اكتب لي خطّك، فكتب: بسم الله الرّحمن الرّحيم، هذا ما ابتاع إسـمـاعـيــل مـن العبد أحمد ابن الرفاعي ضامناً على كرم الله له قصراً في الجنَّة، يحُدُّه حدود؛ الأوَّل: لجنَّة عدن الثَّاني: لجنَّة المأوى، الثالث: لجنة الخلد، الرابع: لجنة الفردوس بجميع حوره وولدان وفرشه وأشربته وأنهاره وأشجاره عوضاً عن بستانه في الدُّنيا، والله شاهد على ذلك وكفيل، مات إسماعيل؛ دفنت معه الورقة فأصبحوا وإذا مكتوب على قبره: قد وجدنا ما وعدنا ربُّنا حقاً. فلمَّا مات ببلده سنة ثمان وسبعين وخمس مئة، ولم يعقب.
When he performed the pilgrimage, he stood facing the noble prophetic chamber and recited: 'I used to send her (my soul) to kiss the earth for me, so she is my deputy in the state of distance, and now this is the turn of the bodies, so I have come; extend your hand so that my lips may obtain it.' Then the noble hand came out of the grave until he kissed it, and the people were looking at it. And he informed (others) of the time and description of his death, and it was as he said. And he wanted to buy a garden, but its owner refused to sell it except for a palace in Paradise. So he trembled, changed color, and turned pale. Then he said: 'I have bought it from you for that.' The owner said: 'Write me your deed.' So he wrote: 'In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. This is what Isma'il purchased from the servant Ahmad ibn al-Rifa'i, guaranteeing upon Allah's generosity a palace for him in Paradise, bounded by four boundaries: first, the Garden of Eden; second, the Garden of Refuge; third, the Garden of Eternity; fourth, the Garden of Paradise, with all its houris, boys, furnishings, drinks, rivers, and trees, in exchange for his garden in this world. And Allah is witness and guarantor.' Isma'il died; the paper was buried with him, and in the morning they found written on his grave: 'We have found true what our Lord promised us.' Then he died in his town in the year 578 AH, and left no offspring.
Source pages p. 451

Commentary
This passage narrates several miracles (karamat) associated with the Sufi saint Ahmad al-Rifa'i. The first miracle: while performing the Hajj, he recites a poem expressing his longing for the Prophet, and the Prophet's hand emerges from the grave to be kissed, witnessed by many people. This is a classic hagiographic motif affirming the saint's closeness to the Prophet. Second, he accurately predicts his own death. Third, a remarkable transaction: a man refuses to sell a garden except for a palace in Paradise. Ahmad al-Rifa'i accepts, writing a deed guaranteeing the palace on Allah's behalf, listing the four levels of Paradise as the boundaries. After the buyer dies, the deed is buried with him, and a divine inscription appears on the grave confirming the fulfillment of the promise. The passage concludes with the saint's death in 578 AH without heirs, emphasizing his detachment from worldly succession.

يد شريفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Prophet's physical hand literally emerged from the grave as a regular occurrence or that this is a core Islamic doctrine.
Correction: These are hagiographic accounts meant to inspire, not dogmatic claims. Miracles of saints (karamat) are accepted in Sunni Islam but are not part of essential belief.

A) A sum of gold coins

D) A piece of land in exchange

Key Takeaway
Ahmad al-Rifa'i's miracles, including the Prophet's hand from the grave and the heavenly transaction, highlight the special graces Allah grants to His awliya.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When Ahmad recited his poem longing for the Prophet, his soul had kissed the earth from afar, but his body yearned to touch the Prophet's hand. Do you have that same burning desire to be near the Prophet? What is holding you back from nurturing that longing in your daily life? Commit to one act today that increases your love for him.
?
The seller asked for a palace in Paradise, and Ahmad trembled and turned pale. If you were faced with a transaction that required risking your worldly security for the unseen, would you hesitate? Examine your heart: are you willing to trade something you hold dear for the promise of Paradise, or do you cling to this world? Write down one worldly attachment you will surrender to Allah today.
?
The deed was written with Allah as witness and guarantor, and it was honored. Do you live your life as if every promise you make is witnessed by Allah? Is there a covenant you have broken or neglected? Repent and renew your commitment to that promise now.

The Spiritual Journey of Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani
Narrates the early life, asceticism, and encounter with al-Khidr of Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the early life and extreme ascetic practices that shaped Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani's spiritual path, including his encounter with al-Khidr.

Core Idea
Extreme struggle and divine testing mark the path to spiritual perfection.

This passage from al-Manawi's biography introduces one of the most revered saints in Sufism, Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani. It details his lineage, his rigorous self-discipline, and the extraordinary spiritual experiences that prepared him for his role as a spiritual axis. As you read, notice the emphasis on physical hardships and encounters with the unseen.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical context
The passage identifies Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani's lineage and his scholarly status. Notice that he was both a Hanbali jurist and a master of spiritual states.
2
Understand the ascetic practices
The text describes extreme self-denial: wearing rags, walking barefoot, eating minimal food. Reflect on the purpose of these struggles in Sufi training.
These practices are meant to purify the soul.
3
Examine the encounter with al-Khidr
Al-Khidr, a mysterious figure, instructed him to wait for three years. Consider the symbolism of this test of patience and trust.
4
Reflect on the year-long fast and nocturnal experience
He went a year without food, drink, or sleep, and had forty wet dreams in one night. These are extraordinary signs of spiritual struggle and purification.
This shows his complete reliance on Allah.
5
Note the outcome: attainment of perfection
After these trials, he wandered in deserts and mountains until he attained perfection. This is the goal of the spiritual journey.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تراجم رجال التصوف والقطب الرَّبانيُّ الإمامُ سيدي عبد القادر الجيلاني وأتباعه، قوله: (سيدي عبد القادر الجيلاني) قال المناوي في الكتاب المذكور: (هو ابن موسى بن يحيى الجيلاني الحنبلي، كان في الفقه إماماً، وفي التَّصرُّف [لا يسام رفعةً ولا] يسامى. ولد [بجيلان] سنة سبعين وأربع مئة، ونشأ بها حتَّى شب، فسلك طريق القوم، فجدَّ واجتهد، وكابد الأهوال حتّى كان يلف على رأسه خرقة ويلبس جبَّة، ويمشي حافياً، ويتقوَّت بقمامة البقل وورق الخس، ويجاهد نفسه بأنواع الشَّدائد. وأتاه الخضر مرَّة وهو لا يعرفه فقال: اقعد هنا حتّى آتيك، فأقام في ذلك الموضع ثلاث سنين. ومكث [في بدايته] سنة لا يأكل ولا يشرب ولا ينام، واحتلم في ليلة في بدايته في الشّتاء أربعين مرّة، يغتسل لكلِّ مرَّة، ولم يزل على ذلك الحال حتّى طرقه الحال فهام في البراري والجبال إلى أن اتّصف بالكمال. ومن كراماته: أنَّه كان حين رضاعه لا يرضع في رمضان، فكان الناس إذا شكُوا في الهلال رجعوا إليه، وكان الذُّباب لا يصيبه وراثة من جده المصطفى، وأقام أربعين سنة يصلّي الصُّبح بوضوء العشاء، وكان يفتي على مذهب الشافعي وأحمد معاً، فيتعجب علماء العراق من حسن أجوبته.
Biographies of men of Sufism: and the spiritual axis, the imam, my master Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani and his followers. His saying: 'My master Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani' – al-Manawi said in the aforementioned book: 'He is the son of Musa ibn Yahya al-Jilani al-Hanbali. He was an imam in jurisprudence, and in spiritual states he could not be surpassed in rank nor competed with. He was born in Jilan in the year 470 AH, and grew up there until he reached maturity. He took the path of the people (of Sufism), striving and exerting himself, enduring terrors until he would wrap a rag on his head, wear a cloak, walk barefoot, subsist on scraps of vegetables and lettuce leaves, and struggle against his soul with all kinds of hardships. Once al-Khidr came to him while he did not recognize him and said: 'Sit here until I come to you,' so he remained in that place for three years. And he remained [at the beginning of his path] for a year without eating, drinking, or sleeping. In one night at the beginning of his path in winter, he had a wet dream forty times, bathing for each one. He continued in that state until the state (of ecstasy) came to him, and he wandered in deserts and mountains until he attained perfection. Among his miracles: when he was nursing, he would not nurse in Ramadan, so when people doubted the crescent (moon), they would refer to him. Flies would not alight on him, inherited from his grandfather the Chosen One (the Prophet). He prayed the dawn prayer for forty years with the ablution of the night prayer. He would give legal verdicts according to both the Shafi'i and Hanbali schools simultaneously, and the scholars of Iraq would marvel at the excellence of his answers.'
Source pages p. 452

Commentary
This passage provides a biography of the renowned Sufi saint Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani, quoting from al-Manawi. It describes his lineage, birth in Jilan in 470 AH, and his early life. He became a leading scholar in Hanbali jurisprudence and a master of spiritual states. The text emphasizes his extreme ascetic practices: wearing rags, walking barefoot, eating minimal food, and enduring severe hardships. Two extraordinary incidents are mentioned: his encounter with al-Khidr, who told him to wait in one spot for three years, and a year-long fast without food, drink, or sleep. In a single winter night, he had forty wet dreams and bathed each time, illustrating his purity and struggle. His spiritual state eventually overwhelmed him, leading him to wander in wilderness until he attained perfection. The passage then lists his miracles: as an infant, he refused to nurse during Ramadan, so people used him to verify the new moon; flies avoided him due to his inherited connection to the Prophet; he performed the dawn prayer for forty years with the night ablution; and he issued fatwas in two madhhabs simultaneously, amazing scholars. These details highlight his sanctity and the reverence accorded to him in Sufi tradition.

الخضر
التصوف
القطب الرباني

Key Takeaway
The spiritual path demands extreme self-discipline and patience, culminating in divine perfection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read about a man who waited three years without complaint. Where in your life have you abandoned patience when Allah asked you to wait? What is one step you can take today to return to that station of sabr?
?
Al-Jilani walked barefoot and ate scraps to discipline his soul. What comfort in your daily worship—whether physical, emotional, or social—has become a crutch that prevents you from drawing closer to Allah? Name it and decide what you will do about it before you sleep tonight.
?
He was tested with an experience (the forty baths in one night) that purified him through extreme humility. What is one area of your life where you have avoided the discomfort of repentance and purification? Will you let that pride stand, or will you submit to the cleansing process—even if it costs you your dignity?

The Miracles of Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani
Lists four miracles of Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani, demonstrating his sainthood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will learn about the miracles attributed to Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani, including his infant fasting, protection from flies, long-term night prayer ablution, and dual juristic authority.

Core Idea
Miracles confirm the saint's closeness to Allah and his prophetic inheritance.

After describing his rigorous asceticism, the passage turns to the supernatural gifts bestowed upon Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani. These miracles—refusing milk in Ramadan, being untouched by flies, performing dawn prayers with the night's ablution for decades, and issuing fatwas in two schools—demonstrate his elevated spiritual rank and his connection to the Prophet Muhammad. Read this section to see how sainthood is validated through extraordinary signs.

Guided Path
1
Examine the first miracle: fasting as an infant
As a nursing baby, he would not breastfeed during Ramadan. This was taken as a sign so that people consulted him about the new moon.
This emphasizes his purity from infancy.
2
Notice the second miracle: protection from flies
Flies would never land on him, inherited from the Prophet Muhammad. This is a sign of spiritual honor.
It links him directly to the Prophet.
3
Observe the third miracle: continuous ablution
He performed the dawn prayer for forty years with the same ablution he had made for the night prayer. This shows his constant state of purity and devotion.
Forty years indicates his unwavering focus.
4
Understand the fourth miracle: dual fatwa authority
He would issue legal verdicts according to both Shafi'i and Hanbali schools simultaneously, amazing scholars. This demonstrates his profound knowledge.
5
Reflect on the purpose of such miracles
These miracles are seen as signs of Allah's favor and serve to confirm his sainthood and authority. They are not meant to be literal proofs but spiritual endorsements.

Biographies of men of Sufism: and the spiritual axis, the imam, my master Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani and his followers. His saying: 'My master Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani' – al-Manawi said in the aforementioned book: 'He is the son of Musa ibn Yahya al-Jilani al-Hanbali. He was an imam in jurisprudence, and in spiritual states he could not be surpassed in rank nor competed with. He was born in Jilan in the year 470 AH, and grew up there until he reached maturity. He took the path of the people (of Sufism), striving and exerting himself, enduring terrors until he would wrap a rag on his head, wear a cloak, walk barefoot, subsist on scraps of vegetables and lettuce leaves, and struggle against his soul with all kinds of hardships. Once al-Khidr came to him while he did not recognize him and said: 'Sit here until I come to you,' so he remained in that place for three years. And he remained [at the beginning of his path] for a year without eating, drinking, or sleeping. In one night at the beginning of his path in winter, he had a wet dream forty times, bathing for each one. He continued in that state until the state (of ecstasy) came to him, and he wandered in deserts and mountains until he attained perfection. Among his miracles: when he was nursing, he would not nurse in Ramadan, so when people doubted the crescent (moon), they would refer to him. Flies would not alight on him, inherited from his grandfather the Chosen One (the Prophet). He prayed the dawn prayer for forty years with the ablution of the night prayer. He would give legal verdicts according to both the Shafi'i and Hanbali schools simultaneously, and the scholars of Iraq would marvel at the excellence of his answers.'

Commentary
This passage provides a biography of the renowned Sufi saint Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani, quoting from al-Manawi. It describes his lineage, birth in Jilan in 470 AH, and his early life. He became a leading scholar in Hanbali jurisprudence and a master of spiritual states. The text emphasizes his extreme ascetic practices: wearing rags, walking barefoot, eating minimal food, and enduring severe hardships. Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles of saints are superstitions or fairy tales.
Correction: In Islamic tradition, miracles (karamat) are real supernatural events granted by Allah to His righteous servants as a sign of their status. They are accepted by mainstream Sunni scholars and are distinct from the miracles of prophets.

?

?
He maintained the state of ablution from Isha to Fajr for forty years. Think about your own focus and sincerity in worship: when you pray, do you truly guard your heart until the next prayer? What one change can you make this week to bring more spiritual continuity into your daily prayers?
?
The scholars of Iraq were amazed at his ability to give rulings from two different madhhabs with excellence. Are you content with simplicity in your religion, or are you eager to deepen your knowledge until even those who know more are amazed? The Life and Miracles of Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani
Introduces Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani's lineage, asceticism, and early miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the remarkable life and miracles of Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani as recorded by al-Munawi, focusing on his extreme asceticism and spiritual states.

Core Idea
A saint's journey to God may involve extraordinary struggles and divine favors.

This passage from al-Sawi's commentary introduces one of the most revered figures in Islamic spirituality: Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani. Al-Munawi's account highlights not only his scholarly stature but also the extreme ascetic practices and miraculous events that marked his path. As you read, consider how these stories illustrate the concept of sainthood (wilaya) and the divine support given to sincere seekers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Let the narrative of al-Munawi come through without interruption.
2
Identify key stages
Notice the sequence: his lineage, early asceticism, encounter with Khidr, extreme spiritual efforts, and miracles. Each stage reveals a facet of his sainthood.
The passage moves from physical hardships to supernatural events.
3
Reflect on the miracles
The miracles include his nursing instinct, protection from flies, lengthy ablution consistency, and dual-school fatwas. Ask: what do these teach about divine support for saints?
These are not random but connected to his spiritual station.
4
Address the misunderstanding
The common misunderstanding is that these extreme practices are required for all. The passage shows they were particular to his state, not a general rule.
Sainthood is varied; not every seeker must replicate these.

والقطب الرَّبانيُّ الإمامُ سيدي عبد القادر الجيلاني وأتباعه، قوله : (سيدي عبد القادر الجيلاني قال المناوي في الكتاب المذكور: (هو ابن موسى بن يحيى الجيلاني الحنبلي، كان في الفقه إماماً، وفي التَّصرُّف [ لا يسام رفعةً و] لا يسامى . ولد [ بجيلان] سنة سبعين وأربع مئة ، ونشأ بها حتَّى شب، فسلك طريق القوم، فجدَّ واجتهد، وكابد الأهوال حتّى كان يلف على رأسه خرقة ويلبس جبَّة، ويمشي حافياً، ويتقوَّت بقمامة البقل وورق الخس، ويجاهد نفسه بأنواع الشَّدائد . وأتاه الخضر مرَّة وهو لا يعرفه فقال : اقعد هنا حتّى آتيك، فأقام في ذلك الموضع ثلاث سنين . ومكث [في بدايته] سنة لا يأكل ولا يشرب ولا ينام، واحتلم في ليلة في بدايته في الشّتاء أربعين مرّة، يغتسل لكلِّ مرَّة، ولم يزل على ذلك الحال حتّى طرقه الحال فهام في البراري والجبال إلى أن اتّصف بالكمال . ومن كراماته : أنَّه كان حين رضاعه لا يرضع في رمضان، فكان الناس إذا شكُوا في الهلال رجعوا إليه، وكان الذُّباب لا يصيبه وراثة من جده المصطفى ، وأقام أربعين سنة يصلّي الصُّبح بوضوء العشاء، وكان يفتي على مذهب الشافعي وأحمد معاً، فيتعجب علماء العراق من حسن أجوبته .
And the spiritual pole, the Imam, my master Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani and his followers. His statement: (my master Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani) al-Munawi said in the aforementioned book: (He is the son of Musa ibn Yahya al-Jilani al-Hanbali. He was in jurisprudence an imam, and in spiritual states [he is not approached in elevation and] not vied with. He was born in [Jilan] in the year 470 AH, and grew up there until he matured. He then traversed the path of the people [of tasawwuf], so he strove and exerted himself, and endured terrors until he would wrap a rag on his head, wear a cloak, walk barefoot, subsist on vegetable scraps and lettuce leaves, and fight his soul with all kinds of hardships. Al-Khidr came to him once while he did not know him and said: Sit here until I come to you, so he stayed in that place for three years. He remained [in his beginning] for a year without eating, drinking, or sleeping. He had a nocturnal emission in one night of his beginning in winter forty times, bathing for each time. He continued in that state until the state struck him, so he roamed the deserts and mountains until he was characterized by perfection. Among his miracles: that during his nursing he would not suckle during Ramadan, so when people doubted about the crescent moon, they would refer to him. Flies would not land on him, an inheritance from his grandfather the Chosen One. He performed the dawn prayer for forty years with the ablution of the night prayer. He gave legal opinions according to both the Shafi'i and Hanbali schools simultaneously, so the scholars of Iraq marveled at the excellence of his answers.)
Source pages p. 452

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry on Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani, quoting al-Munawi. It begins by identifying him as the spiritual pole and imam. Then it describes his lineage and status. It details his ascetic practices: wearing rags, walking barefoot, eating scraps, fasting, staying awake, enduring repeated ritual impurity and bathing in winter, and wandering in seclusion. Then it lists miracles: his refusal to nurse in Ramadan (used to confirm the moon), flies not landing on him (inherited from the Prophet), performing dawn prayer with night ablution for forty years, and giving fatwas in two schools simultaneously, impressing Iraqi scholars. The passage emphasizes his piety and divine favor.

The False Divine Light: Recognizing Satan's Deception
Narrates a miracle of recognizing Satan disguised as divine light.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sheikh Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani discerned a satanic deception through his adherence to Islamic law.

Core Idea
Satan's trick is to relax divine law; true sainthood is grounded in sharia.

This story illustrates a critical principle in Islamic spirituality: not every spiritual experience is from God. Sheikh Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani encountered a dazzling light that claimed to be God, but he immediately recognized it as Satan because it offered to make forbidden things permissible. This lesson explores how firm knowledge of sharia protects believers from deception.

Guided Path
1
Read the story of the false light
Read the first part of the passage where the light appears and claims divinity.
2
Identify the means of recognition
Note what the voice said that made the sheikh recognize it as Satan.
It said 'I have made permissible for you forbidden things.'
3
Understand the role of fiqh
Satan admits that the sheikh escaped through his fiqh (jurisprudence). Think about why a deep understanding of sharia is a protection.
This shows the importance of knowledge before experience.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how this story informs your own approach to spiritual experiences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورأى مرَّة نوراً ملأ الأفق، ونودى منه : أنا ربُّك، وقد أبحث لك المحرَّمات فقال : اخسأ يا لعين فانقلب النُّور دخاناً وظلاماً، فقال: نجوت منّي بفقهك [ في إحكام منازلاتك]، وقد أضللت بهذا سبعين صديقاً، فسئل : بم عرفت أنَّه الشَّيطان؟ قال: بقوله : أبحث لك المحرمات . وسقطت عليه وهو يدرس حيَّة، ففرّ من حضر، فدخلت في ذيله وخرجت من طوقه، والتفَّتْ على عنقه فلم يقطع كلامه ولم يتغيَّر، ثمَّ تكلّمه قامت بين يديه بكلام لا يفهم وانصرفت فسئل [عنها]، فقال: قالت : اختبرت عدة من الأولياء فلم أجد كثباتك، فقلت : ما أنت إلَّا دويبة يحركّك القضاء والقدر، وكلامه ومناقبه أفردت بالتأليف، مات سنة نيف وستين وخمس مئة ببغداد ، له وعنا به ) (۱) .
And he once saw a light filling the horizon, and from it was called out: 'I am your Lord, and I have made permissible for you forbidden things.' So he said: 'Be gone, O accursed one!' Then the light turned into smoke and darkness. Then it said: 'You have escaped me through your fiqh (jurisprudence) [in the perfection of your states], and I have led astray seventy friends by this.' He was asked: 'How did you know it was Satan?' He said: 'By his saying: I have made permissible for you forbidden things.' And a snake fell on him while he was teaching, so those present fled. It entered his cloak and came out of his collar, and coiled around his neck, but he did not stop his speech and did not change. Then after he spoke, it stood before him speaking unintelligibly and went away. He was asked about it, and he said: 'It said: I have tested many saints and found no one with your steadfastness. I said: You are nothing but a creature moved by predestination and decree.' His speech and his virtues have been compiled separately. He died in the year 561 AH in Baghdad. May God be pleased with him.)
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This passage recounts two miracles of Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani. First, a deceptive light claims to be God offering to make forbidden things permissible. The saint immediately recognizes it as Satan because Satan would propose relaxing divine law. He rebukes it, and the light turns to smoke. Satan admits that the saint's fiqh (understanding of divine law) protected him, and that he had misled seventy friends with this trick. The lesson is that true sainthood is grounded in sharia and tawhid, not in emotional states. Second, a snake falls on him while he is teaching. Others flee, but he remains calm. The snake wraps around his neck but doesn't interrupt his lesson. Later it speaks, confessing that it tested many saints but found no one as steadfast. The saint attributes this to qadar: the snake is merely a creature moved by God's decree. This shows his profound reliance on divine predestination and his unshakable trust in God. The passage ends with his death year and a note that his spiritual states have been collected in a separate work.

Key Terms
الشيطان
الفقه
كرامات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any powerful spiritual experience must be from God.
Correction: This story shows that even a light filling the horizon can be from Satan if it contradicts sharia.

Checkpoint
What did the voice in the light claim it would do?
A) Grant paradise
B) Make forbidden things permissible
C) Show the future
D) Give wealth

Key Takeaway
Adherence to Islamic law is the primary safeguard against spiritual deception.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever followed a spiritual feeling or experience that contradicted what you know to be right from Islamic law? How did you justify it to yourself? What will you do when the next such impulse comes?
?
When someone offers you a shortcut to piety—a way that seems easier or more enlightened but relaxes a clear command of Allah—will you have the courage to say 'be gone' as the sheikh did, or will you rationalize it?
?
If you were in a state of overwhelming spiritual experience, would you be able to reject it based solely on its content, even if it feels convincing? What is the state of your fiqh right now—is it strong enough to protect you?

The Snake: Steadfastness and Trust in Divine Decree
Narrates a miracle of calmness under threat from a snake.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sheikh Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani's complete trust in Allah's decree gave him unshakable calm when a snake fell on him.

Core Idea
Complete trust in Allah's decree makes a saint fearless even in danger.

The second miracle in this passage shows the sheikh's extraordinary composure when a snake falls on him while he is teaching. Others flee, but he remains calm, and the snake eventually speaks and admits his steadfastness. This lesson explores how reliance on qadar (divine decree) produces true courage.

Guided Path
1
Read the snake story
Read the second part of the passage describing the snake incident.
2
Observe the sheikh's reaction
Note that he did not stop speaking or show fear. Contrast with others who fled.
3
Understand his explanation
The sheikh later says the snake is just a creature moved by qadar. How does this perspective remove fear?
4
Reflect on tawakkul
Think about how trusting Allah's decree can help you face difficulties.

Biography of Ahmad al-Badawi from al-Munawi
Introduces Ahmad al-Badawi's lineage, birth, and early studies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key biographical details of Ahmad al-Badawi as recorded by al-Munawi, including his lineage, birth, and early religious education.

Core Idea
Ahmad al-Badawi's noble lineage and early piety set the stage for his later sainthood.

Before we explore the theological contributions of Sayyid Ahmad al-Badawi, we first encounter his biographical sketch from al-Munawi. This passage establishes his credentials as a sharif (descendant of the Prophet) and his foundational religious training. It provides the background needed to appreciate his later role as a major Sufi figure.

Guided Path
1

Read the Arabic text and its English translation. Note the flow from lineage to birth, upbringing, and Hajj.
The passage begins with the phrase 'قوله' indicating it is a quotation within the commentary.

List the key facts: his full lineage, birth year and location, his father's migration, his education, and the Hajj journey.
3
Understand the significance of 'sharif'
The title 'al-sharif' indicates descent from the Prophet. This is a mark of honor and spiritual authority in Islamic tradition.
4
Connect to broader context
Ahmad al-Badawi is a major figure in Sufism. His early life in Fes and Mecca shaped his spiritual development.

قوله : (السَّيِّد أحمد البدوي : قال المناوي فيه أيضاً : (هو ابن علي بن إبراهيم بن محمد بن أبي بكر البدوي الشَّريف الحسيب النسيب، أصله من بني بري ؛ قبيلة من عربان الشَّام، ثم سكن والده المغرب. ضي عنه ولد بفاس سنة ست وتسعين وخمس مئة، ونشأ بها وحفظ القرآن، وقرأ شيئاً من فقه الشافعي . وحجَّ أبوه به وبإخوته سنة تسع وست مئة، وأقاموا بمكة، ومات بها
His statement: (Sayyid Ahmad al-Badawi: al-Munawi said about him also: (He is the son of Ali ibn Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr al-Badawi, the noble, of good lineage and descent. His origin is from the Banu Birri, a tribe of the Arabs of Syria. Then his father settled in the Maghreb. May God be pleased with him. He was born in Fes in the year 596 AH, grew up there, memorized the Quran, and studied some of Shafi'i fiqh. His father performed Hajj with him and his brothers in the year 609 AH, and they stayed in Mecca, and he died there.)
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This passage provides the biographical entry for Ahmad al-Badawi, quoting al-Munawi. It begins by identifying him as Sayyid Ahmad al-Badawi, a sharif (descendant of the Prophet). His lineage traces back to Abu Bakr al-Badawi, and his tribe is Banu Birri from Syrian Arabs. His father moved to the Maghreb. Ahmad al-Badawi was born in Fes in 596 AH (1200 CE), grew up there, memorized the Quran, and studied some Shafi'i fiqh. His father took him and his brothers for Hajj in 609 AH, and they settled in Mecca, where he died. The entry establishes his noble lineage and early religious education.

Recognizing the Devil's Deception
Al-Jilani identifies the devil through his offer to legalize prohibitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how spiritual discernment rooted in knowledge of divine law enables a saint to recognize and reject satanic deception.

Core Idea
True spiritual knowledge prevents even disguised devilry from succeeding.

The great saint Abdul Qadir al-Jilani was once tested by a vision that appeared divine. His immediate rejection of a voice claiming to be God, based on its invitation to legalize prohibitions, reveals a key principle: any claim to divine communication that contradicts the revealed law is automatically false. This story illustrates the critical role of fiqh (Islamic jurisprudence) in safeguarding spiritual experience.

Guided Path
1
Read the account of the light
Read the Arabic passage describing the light filling the horizon and the voice claiming to be God. Notice the specific promise it makes.
Mark how the voice says 'I will legalize for you prohibitions.'
2
Understand al-Jilani's response
He immediately says 'Begone, O accursed one!' – showing he recognized the voice as the devil without hesitation.
His response is based on the content, not a feeling.
3
Identify the criterion
When asked how he knew, he replied: 'By his saying: I will legalize for you prohibitions.' The devil offers to make lawful what Allah has made unlawful.
This is a key theological principle: true revelation does not contradict established law.
4
Reflect on the devil's admission
The devil admits that al-Jilani's knowledge of fiqh saved him, and that he had misled seventy saints through this trick.
Notice that even saints can be deceived without proper knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورأى مرَّة نوراً ملأ الأفق، ونودى منه : أنا ربُّك، وقد أبحث لك المحرَّمات فقال : اخسأ يا لعين فانقلب النُّور دخاناً وظلاماً، فقال: نجوت منّي بفقهك [ في إحكام منازلاتك]، وقد أضللت بهذا سبعين صديقاً، فسئل : بم عرفت أنَّه الشَّيطان؟ قال: بقوله : أبحث لك المحرمات . وسقطت عليه وهو يدرس حيَّة، ففرّ من حضر، فدخلت في ذيله وخرجت من طوقه، والتفَّتْ على عنقه فلم يقطع كلامه ولم يتغيَّر، ثمَّ تكلّمه قامت بين يديه بكلام لا يفهم وانصرفت فسئل [عنها]، فقال: قالت : اختبرت عدة من الأولياء فلم أجد كثباتك، فقلت : ما أنت إلَّا دويبة يحركّك القضاء والقدر، وكلامه ومناقبه أفردت بالتأليف، مات سنة نيف وستين وخمس مئة ببغداد ، له وعنا به ) (۱) .
And he once saw a light filling the horizon, and it was called out from it: 'I am your Lord, and I will legalize for you prohibitions.' So he said: 'Begone, O accursed one!' And the light turned into smoke and darkness. It said: 'You have escaped me through your jurisprudence [in the exactness of your stations], and I have led astray through this seventy saints.' So he was asked: 'How did you know it was the devil?' He said: 'By his saying: "I will legalize for you prohibitions."' And a snake fell upon him while he was teaching, and those present fled. It entered into his garment and came out from his collar, and coiled around his neck, but he did not stop speaking nor change his expression. Then when he finished speaking, it stood before him speaking in an unintelligible language and departed. So he was asked about it, and he said: 'It said: I have tested several saints and found no one as steadfast as you. I replied: You are nothing but a creature moved by divine decree and predestination.' His words and merits have been compiled into a book. He died in the year approximately 560 AH in Baghdad, may Allah be pleased with him and with us through him.) (1).
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This passage narrates two miraculous incidents in the life of the great Sufi saint Abdul Qadir al-Jilani, demonstrating his spiritual discernment and unshakable composure. The first incident: he sees a light filling the horizon and hears a voice claiming to be his Lord, offering to legalize prohibitions for him. Al-Jilani immediately recognizes the voice as that of the devil because it promises to make lawful what Allah has forbidden — a true Lord would not contradict His own law. This shows his deep grounding in fiqh. The devil then admits that al-Jilani's knowledge of fiqh saved him, and that he had misled seventy others through this trick. The second incident: a snake falls on him while he is teaching. Everyone flees, but the snake enters his clothes and coils around his neck without disturbing him. After he finishes speaking, the snake speaks to him in an unintelligible language, and when asked, al-Jilani explains that the snake said it had tested many saints but found none as steadfast as him, and he replied that the snake is merely a creature subject to divine decree. The passage concludes with a note that his words and merits have been compiled, and he died in Baghdad around 560 AH.

Key Terms
الشيطان
المحرمات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think al-Jilani's refusal of the light was a rejection of direct divine communication, but he recognized it based on content contradicting Islamic law.
Correction: Al-Jilani did not reject the possibility of divine communication; he rejected the specific claim because the content contradicted the established law of Allah.

Checkpoint
How did Abdul Qadir al-Jilani recognize that the voice from the light was the devil?
A) The voice sounded deceptive
B) The voice offered to legalize prohibitions
C) The light turned to smoke
D) He had prior warning from angels

Key Takeaway
Spiritual discernment requires knowledge of divine law; any claim that contradicts the law is automatically from the devil.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been tempted to justify a sin by making it seem permissible? How does al-Jilani's immediate rejection challenge your own compromises? What specific step will you take this week to align your actions strictly with Allah's boundaries?
?
When you encounter a spiritual experience—whether a dream, a feeling, or a vision—do you test it against Allah's law, or do you let the experience override your knowledge? What would you do if something felt overwhelmingly divine but contradicted what you know?
?
Al-Jilani recognized the devil because of his knowledge of fiqh. Are you investing in sacred knowledge, or are you relying on feelings alone? What one concrete action will you take today to deepen your understanding of Allah's commands and prohibitions?

Steadfastness in the Face of Danger
Al-Jilani's composure when a snake coiled around him while teaching

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the profound trust in divine decree that enables a saint to remain unshaken even in life-threatening situations.

Core Idea
Absolute reliance on Allah's decree frees one from fear of creation.

A snake once fell on Abdul Qadir al-Jilani while he was teaching, causing those present to flee. The snake entered his clothes and coiled around his neck, but al-Jilani continued his lesson without interruption. This story demonstrates the saint's unshakeable composure, rooted in his conviction that everything—including the snake—is subject to Allah's will and decree.

Guided Path
1
Read the snake incident
Read the Arabic passage describing the snake falling, the people fleeing, and the snake entering and coiling around al-Jilani.
Note his complete lack of reaction.
2
Observe his response
He did not stop speaking nor change his expression. This shows extraordinary composure.
3
Understand his reply to the snake
After teaching, the snake spoke and al-Jilani later explained: he told the snake it is merely a creature moved by divine decree and predestination.
This reveals his worldview: nothing acts independently of Allah.
4
Connect to tawakkul
His trust in Allah (tawakkul) was so complete that even a snake coiled around his neck did not disturb him.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورأى مرَّة نوراً ملأ الأفق، ونودى منه : أنا ربُّك، وقد أبحث لك المحرَّمات فقال : اخسأ يا لعين فانقلب النُّور دخاناً وظلاماً، فقال: نجوت منّي بفقهك [ في إحكام منازلاتك]، وقد أضللت بهذا سبعين صديقاً، فسئل : بم عرفت أنَّه الشَّيطان؟ قال: بقوله : أبحث لك المحرمات . وسقطت عليه وهو يدرس حيَّة، ففرّ من حضر، فدخلت في ذيله وخرجت من طوقه، والتفَّتْ على عنقه فلم يقطع كلامه ولم يتغيَّر، ثمَّ تكلّمه قامت بين يديه بكلام لا يفهم وانصرفت فسئل [عنها]، فقال: قالت : اختبرت عدة من الأولياء فلم أجد كثباتك، فقلت : ما أنت إلَّا دويبة يحركّك القضاء والقدر، وكلامه ومناقبه أفردت بالتأليف، مات سنة نيف وستين وخمس مئة ببغداد ، له وعنا به ) (۱) .
And he once saw a light filling the horizon, and it was called out from it: 'I am your Lord, and I will legalize for you prohibitions.' So he said: 'Begone, O accursed one!' And the light turned into smoke and darkness. It said: 'You have escaped me through your jurisprudence [in the exactness of your stations], and I have led astray through this seventy saints.' So he was asked: 'How did you know it was the devil?' He said: 'By his saying: "I will legalize for you prohibitions."' And a snake fell upon him while he was teaching, and those present fled. It entered into his garment and came out from his collar, and coiled around his neck, but he did not stop speaking nor change his expression. Then when he finished speaking, it stood before him speaking in an unintelligible language and departed. So he was asked about it, and he said: 'It said: I have tested several saints and found no one as steadfast as you. I replied: You are nothing but a creature moved by divine decree and predestination.' His words and merits have been compiled into a book. He died in the year approximately 560 AH in Baghdad, may Allah be pleased with him and with us through him.) (1).

Commentary
This passage narrates two miraculous incidents in the life of the great Sufi saint Abdul Qadir al-Jilani, demonstrating his spiritual discernment and unshakable composure. The first incident: he sees a light filling the horizon and hears a voice claiming to be his Lord, offering to legalize prohibitions for him. Al-Jilani immediately recognizes the voice as that of the devil because it promises to make lawful what Allah has forbidden — a true Lord would not contradict His own law. This shows his deep grounding in fiqh. The devil then admits that al-Jilani's knowledge of fiqh saved him, and that he had misled seventy others through this trick. The second incident: a snake falls on him while he is teaching. Everyone flees, but the snake enters his clothes and coils around his neck without disturbing him. After he finishes speaking, the snake speaks to him in an unintelligible language, and when asked, al-Jilani explains that the snake said it had tested many saints but found none as steadfast as him, and he replied that the snake is merely a creature subject to divine decree. The passage concludes with a note that his words and merits have been compiled, and he died in Baghdad around 560 AH.

Key Terms
الحية
القضاء والقدر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think al-Jilani's lack of fear was due to magic or supernatural powers, but it stemmed from his deep faith in divine decree.
Correction: His composure was a result of his unwavering trust in Allah and his recognition that the snake's actions were predetermined by Allah.

Checkpoint
What did al-Jilani tell the snake when it tested him?

B) 'You are nothing but a creature moved by divine decree.'
C) 'Go away in the name of Allah.'

Key Takeaway
True reliance on Allah (tawakkul) removes fear of creation, as every creature is merely moved by divine decree.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you next face a sudden threat or cause for panic, will you remember that the thing you fear is merely a creature moved by Allah's decree? How can you train yourself to react like al-Jilani rather than fleeing like the others?
?
Al-Jilani did not even change his expression. In your daily life, what small anxieties reveal that you still attribute independent power to people or events? What step will you take tomorrow to weaken that false belief?
?
The snake spoke only after the lesson ended. Are you willing to trust Allah's timing and remain steadfast even when the trial is still unfolding, or do you demand immediate relief? What would it cost you to truly wait upon His decree?

The Life and Spiritual Path of Ahmad al-Badawi
Biographical account of Ahmad al-Badawi's lineage, practices, and spiritual encounters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key events and spiritual practices of Ahmad al-Badawi's life as recorded in Sunni hagiography.

Core Idea
Ahmad al-Badawi's total reliance on God set him apart among saints.

This passage from al-Munawi's biographical dictionary introduces one of Egypt's most revered Sufi saints. His life is marked by extreme asceticism, miraculous encounters, and unwavering trust in Allah. Let us explore his lineage, his practices, and the famous story of his refusal of keys from two great saints.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography carefully
Read the full Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of Ahmad al-Badawi's life story. Note the key events: birth, education, migration, and spiritual states.
Pay attention to the names and places mentioned.
2
Examine his distinctive practices
Notice his constant wearing of the litham (face veil), his silence, his long fasts, and his fixed gaze. What do these indicate about his spiritual state?
These practices are signs of his absorption in God.
3
Understand the encounter with al-Jilani and al-Rifa'i
When offered the keys of the world by two great saints, al-Badawi refused, saying he would only take the key from the Opener (Allah). This shows his complete trust in God alone.
This is a key moment highlighting his tawakkul.
4
Reflect on his settlement in Tanta
He stayed on a rooftop for twelve years without leaving. His occasional loud cries indicate the intensity of his spiritual states.
Tanta remains a major pilgrimage site today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (السَّيِّد أحمد البدوي : قال المناوي فيه أيضاً : (هو ابن علي بن إبراهيم بن محمد بن أبي بكر البدوي الشَّريف الحسيب النسيب، أصله من بني بري ؛ قبيلة من عربان الشَّام، ثم سكن والده المغرب. ضي عنه ولد بفاس سنة ست وتسعين وخمس مئة، ونشأ بها وحفظ القرآن، وقرأ شيئاً من فقه الشافعي . وحجَّ أبوه به وبإخوته سنة تسع وست مئة، وأقاموا بمكة، ومات بها أبوه سنة سبع وعشرين وسنّ مئة، ودفن بالمعلا . وعرف بالبدوي للزومه اللثام، ولبس لثامين فلم يفارقهما، ولم يتزوّج قط، واشتهر بالعطاب؛ لكثرة عطبه من يؤذيه، ثمَّ لزم الصمت، فكان لا يتكلم إلا بإشارة، وتوله، ثم حصلت له جمعيَّة على الحقِّ فاستغرق إلى الأبد، وكان عظيم الفتوة. قال المتبولي : قال لي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «ما في أولياء مـصـر بـعـد بن إدريس أكبر فتوة منه، ثمَّ نفيسة، ثمَّ شرف الدين الكردي، ثمَّ محمد المنوفي» انتهى . وكان يمكث أربعين يوماً لا يأكل ولا يشرب ولا ينام وأكثر أوقاته شاخص ببصره نحو السَّماء وعيناه كالجمرتين ، ثم يسمع هاتفاً يقول ثلاثاً : قم واطلب مطلع الشمس، فإذا وصلته فاطلب مغربها، وسر إلى طندتا فيها مقامك أيُّها الفتى فسار إلى العراق فتلقاه العارفان الكيلاني والرفاعي فقالا يا أحمد؛ مفاتيح العراق والهند واليمن، والمشرق والمغرب بيدينا، فاختر أيُّها شئت، فقال: لا آخذ المفتاح إلا من يد الفتّاح. ثم رحل إلى مصر فتلقاه الظاهر بيبرس بعسكره، وأكرمه وعظمه، فدخلها سنة أربع وثلاثين وست مئة . فأقام بطندتا على سطح دار لا يفارقه ليلاً ولا نهاراً اثنتي عشرة سنة، وإذا عرض له الحال صاح صياحاً عظيماً .
His statement: (Sayyid Ahmad al-Badawi: al-Munawi also said about him: He is ibn Ali ibn Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr al-Badawi, the noble and high-born sharif, his origin is from Bani Bari, a tribe of the Bedouins of Syria, then his father settled in Morocco. May Allah be pleased with him. He was born in Fez in the year 596 AH, and grew up there, memorized the Quran, and studied some Shafi'i fiqh. His father performed Hajj with him and his brothers in 609 AH, and they stayed in Mecca. His father died there in 627 AH and was buried in al-Ma'la. He was known as al-Badawi due to his constant wearing of the litham (face veil), and he wore two veils and never parted from them. He never married. He was known as al-Atab (the destroyer) because of how often he destroyed those who harmed him. Then he adhered to silence, and would only speak by gesture, and he became ecstatic. Then he attained a state of total absorption in the Truth and became absorbed into eternity. He was great in chivalry (futuwwa). Al-Mutawalli said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said to me: 'Among the saints of Egypt after Ibn Idris, there is none greater in futuwwa than him, then Nafisa, then Sharaf al-Din al-Kurdi, then Muhammad al-Manufi.' End. He would remain forty days without eating, drinking, or sleeping, and most of the time his gaze would be fixed towards the sky, his eyes like two embers. Then he would hear a caller saying three times: 'Arise and seek the rising place of the sun, and when you reach it, seek its setting place, and travel to Tanta, for there is your station, O youth.' So he traveled to Iraq, and the two knowers al-Kilani and al-Rifa'i met him and said: 'O Ahmad, the keys of Iraq, India, Yemen, the East and the West are in our hands, choose whichever you wish.' He said: 'I will not take the key except from the hand of the Opener (al-Fattah).' Then he traveled to Egypt, and al-Zahir Baybars met him with his army, honored and magnified him. He entered it (Egypt) in the year 634 AH. He stayed on the roof of a house in Tanta, not leaving it night or day for twelve years. And when a state overwhelmed him, he would cry out with a great cry.
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed biography of Sayyid Ahmad al-Badawi, a major Sufi saint. It begins by outlining his noble lineage as a sharif, his birth in Fez (Morocco) in 596 AH, his early education including memorizing the Quran and studying Shafi'i fiqh. His family performed Hajj and settled in Mecca, where his father died. Al-Badawi was known for always wearing the litham (face veil), hence his epithet 'al-Badawi.' He never married. He was also called 'al-Atab' because he would destroy those who harmed him. Later, he took a vow of silence, communicating only by gestures, and experienced spiritual ecstasy ('tawalla'), eventually achieving a state of complete absorption in God (jammiyya 'ala al-haqq). The passage then quotes al-Mutawalli, who reports a hadith from the Prophet praising al-Badawi's futuwwa (chivalry) as the greatest among Egyptian saints after Ibn Idris. It describes his extreme asceticism: forty days without food, drink, or sleep, with eyes fixed skyward. A heavenly caller directed him to travel to Tanta via Iraq. In Iraq, he met the great saints Abdul Qadir al-Jilani and Ahmad al-Rifa'i, who offered him the keys of the entire world, but he refused, saying he would only take the key from the Opener (God). He then went to Egypt, received honor from Sultan Baybars, and settled in Tanta, where he remained on a rooftop for twelve years, occasionally crying out loudly when overcome by spiritual states.

Key Terms
السيد أحمد البدوي
البدوي
اللثام
العطاب
الفتوة
الجمعية على الحق
طندتا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ahmad al-Badawi refused the keys from al-Jilani and al-Rifa'i because he did not respect them.
Correction: He refused because he wanted to rely solely on God (al-Fattah), not because of any disrespect. This shows his absolute tawakkul.

Checkpoint
Why did Ahmad al-Badawi refuse the keys offered by al-Kilani and al-Rifa'i?
A) He did not trust them
B) He already had the keys
C) He said he only takes the key from the Opener (Allah)
D) He was not interested in worldly power

Key Takeaway
Ahmad al-Badawi's life exemplifies complete trust in God, extreme asceticism, and spiritual absorption, culminating in his lasting legacy in Tanta.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When faced with a shortcut to success offered by influential people, as al-Badawi was offered the keys of the world by two great saints, do you have enough trust in Allah to refuse and wait for His direct provision? What 'keys' are you tempted to accept right now?
?
Al-Badawi spent forty days without food, drink, or sleep, his gaze fixed on the sky. If you were to try even a fraction of this discipline, what would it reveal about your attachment to bodily comforts and your reliance on Allah's sustenance?
?
He left his homeland and lived on a rooftop for twelve years, rarely speaking. Is there a path of sacrifice or solitude that Allah is calling you to, but you avoid because it demands total dependence on Him? What is holding you back?

The Early Life and Character of Ahmad al-Badawi
Opening biographical details and a prophetic praise for al-Badawi's futuwwa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the origins of Ahmad al-Badawi's nickname, his distinctive practices like wearing the litham, his adoption of silence, and his high rank in spiritual chivalry as attested by the Prophet.

Core Idea
Ahmad al-Badawi's holiness was marked by extreme detachment and silent devotion.

This lesson introduces the saint Ahmad al-Badawi, focusing on his early life, his famous face veil, his renunciation of marriage and speech, and the prophetic praise of his chivalry. It sets the foundation for understanding his later spiritual states.

Guided Path
1
Read the first part of the passage
Read from 'Biographies of the men of Sufism...' up to '...greater chivalry than him.' This covers his father, nickname, and the hadith.
Notice the details about his litham and silence.

Note why he was called al-Badawi (from litham) and al-'Attab (because of harm to those who harmed him). This reflects his spiritual authority.
3
Reflect on his rank in futuwwa

Chivalry here means spiritual nobility and selflessness.

تراجم رجال التصوف
أبوه سنة سبع وعشرين وسنّ مئة، ودفن بالمعلا .
وعرف بالبدوي للزومه اللثام، ولبس لثامين فلم يفارقهما، ولم يتزوّج قط، واشتهر بالعطاب؛ لكثرة عطبه من يؤذيه، ثمَّ لزم الصمت، فكان لا يتكلم إلا بإشارة، وتوله، ثم حصلت له جمعيَّة على الحقِّ فاستغرق إلى الأبد، وكان عظيم الفتوة.

فأقام بطندتا على سطح دار لا يفارقه ليلاً ولا نهاراً اثنتي عشرة سنة، وإذا عرض له الحال صاح صياحاً عظيماً .

وتبعه جمع ؛ منهم عبد العال وعبد المجيد.
ولما دخل طندتا كان بها جمع من الأولياء؛ فمنهم من خرج منها هيبة له ؛ كالشَّيخ حسن الإخناني، فسكن إخنان حتَّى مات، وضريحه بها ظاهر يزار .
ومنهم من مكث ؛ كالشَّيخ سالم المغربي ، وسالَمَ الشَّيخ البدوي، فأقره على حاله حتّى مات بطندتا، وقبره بها مشهور.
ومنهم من أنكر عليه ؛ كصاحب الإيوان العظيم بطندتا المسمى بوجه القمر كان وليّاً كبيراً فثار به الحسد فسلبه ، ومحله الآن بطندتا مأوى الكلاب وليس فيه رائحة صلاح ولا مدد.
وكان الله إذا لبس ثوباً أو عمامة لا يخلعها لا لغسل ولا غيره حتّى تبلى فتبدل، وإذا أمر أحداً من أصحابه بالإقامة في مكان لا يمكنه مخالفته .
وكان يعرف من هو من أولاده بالكشف، ولا يقبل إلَّا من علمه منهم . وكان لا يكشف اللثام عن وجهه، فقال له عبد المجيد : أرني وجهك قال : كل نظرة برجل قال أرنيه فكشف، فمات حالاً. وله كرامات شهيرة جداً منها : قصَّة المرأة التي أسر ولدها الإفرنج، فلاذت به فأحضره في قيوده.

Biographies of the men of Sufism. His father was born in the year twenty-seven and one hundred [AH], and was buried in al-Ma'la. He was known as al-Badawi for his constant wearing of the litham [face veil]; he wore two lithams and never removed them, and he never married at all. He was famous as al-'Attab [the reproacher] because of the great destruction [that befell] whoever harmed him. Then he adhered to silence, and he would not speak except by gesture, and he was devoted. Then a spiritual gathering upon the truth came to him, so he was absorbed into eternity. He had great chivalry. Al-Mutawalli said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said to me: 'Among the saints of Egypt after Ibn Idris, none has greater chivalry than him, then Nafisa, then Sharaf al-Din al-Kurdi, then Muhammad al-Manufi.' End. He would remain forty days without eating, drinking, or sleeping, and most of his time he would stare at the sky with eyes like two embers. Then he would hear a caller saying three times: 'Arise and seek the rising of the sun; when you reach it, seek its setting; and travel to Tanta, for there is your station, O youth.' So he traveled to Iraq, and the two gnostics al-Kilani and al-Rifa'i met him and said: 'O Ahmad, the keys of Iraq, India, Yemen, the east and the west are in our hands; choose whichever you wish.' He said: 'I will not take the key except from the hand of the Opener [al-Fattah].' Then he journeyed to Egypt, and al-Zahir Baybars met him with his army and honored and venerated him. He entered it in the year thirty-four and six hundred [AH]. He resided in Tanta on the roof of a house, never leaving it night or day for twelve years. When a state [of spiritual ecstasy] came over him, he would scream a great scream. A group followed him, among them 'Abd al-'Al and 'Abd al-Majid. When he entered Tanta, there was a group of saints there. Among them were those who left out of awe of him, like Shaykh Hasan al-Ikhnani; he settled in Ikhna until he died, and his tomb there is visible and visited. Among them were those who stayed, like Shaykh Salim al-Maghribi; he made peace with Shaykh al-Badawi, who allowed him to remain as he was until he died in Tanta, and his grave there is well-known. Among them were those who opposed him, like the owner of the great iwan [hall] in Tanta called Wajh al-Qamar; he was a great saint, but envy rose in him and stripped him [of his spiritual state]; his place in Tanta is now a shelter for dogs, and there is in it no trace of righteousness or spiritual support. And [al-Badawi] would, when he wore a garment or a turban, not remove it—neither for washing nor for anything else—until it wore out, then he would replace it. And when he commanded one of his companions to stay in a place, it was impossible for him to disobey. And he would know who among his descendants were [truly his] through spiritual unveiling, and he would accept only those he knew to be [genuine]. And he would not remove the litham from his face. 'Abd al-Majid said to him: 'Show me your face.' He said: 'Every glance is a [fatal] blow.' 'Abd al-Majid said: 'Show me.' So he uncovered [his face], and [Abd al-Majid] died instantly. He had very famous miracles, among them: the story of the woman whose son was captured by the Franks; she sought his refuge, and he brought him in his chains. And a man passed by him carrying a waterskin of milk; he pointed his finger at it, and it split, and [the milk] came out.
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of the Sufi saint Ahmad al-Badawi. It begins by stating his father's death year and burial place, then explains his nickname 'al-Badawi' from his constant wearing of the face veil (litham). It notes that he never married. He was known as al-'Attab because harm would befall those who harmed him. He then adopted silence, communicating only by gesture. The phrase 'tawalla' (devotion) indicates his complete turning to God. He attained a spiritual state of absorption. The author then quotes al-Mutawalli, who reports a hadith from the Prophet praising al-Badawi's chivalry (futuwwa) as the greatest among Egyptian saints after Ibn Idris, followed by Nafisa and others. Next, al-Badawi's extraordinary asceticism is described: forty-day fasts without food, drink, or sleep, staring at the sky. He hears a caller directing him to travel to Tanta, so he goes to Iraq, where the saints al-Kilani and al-Rifa'i offer him keys to various regions, but he refuses, relying solely on Allah. He then goes to Egypt, meets Sultan al-Zahir Baybars, and enters Egypt in 634 AH. He settles in Tanta on a rooftop for twelve years, sometimes screaming in spiritual ecstasy. The passage then describes the reactions of other saints to his arrival: some left out of awe, some stayed in peace, and some opposed him out of envy, losing their spiritual state. The author notes that al-Badawi never changed his clothes until they wore out. His authority over his companions was absolute. He used spiritual unveiling to know his true descendants. When 'Abd al-Majid insisted on seeing his face, al-Badawi warned him, but upon seeing it, 'Abd al-Majid died. Finally, two miracles are mentioned: recovering a captured boy from the Franks and a waterskin splitting at a gesture.

Key Terms
البدوي
اللثام
الفُتُوَّة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that wearing a veil and silence are signs of extreme asceticism without purpose.
Correction: In Sufism, such practices are means to focus on God and achieve spiritual absorption, not ends in themselves.

Checkpoint
Why was Ahmad al-Badawi called 'al-'Attab'?
A) Because he often blamed others.
B) Because harm would befall those who harmed him.
C) Because he wore two lithams.
D) Because he was from the tribe of 'Attab.

Key Takeaway
Ahmad al-Badawi's early spiritual discipline included wearing the litham, silence, and celibacy, and he was praised by the Prophet for his great chivalry.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to love the Prophet, but are you willing to adopt a practice that isolates you from people for His sake? Al-Badawi wore a veil and remained silent for years. What worldly comfort are you unwilling to give up to draw closer to Allah?
?
The Prophet praised al-Badawi for his chivalry. When was the last time you defended someone's honor without any benefit to yourself? Are you willing to be a person of futuwwa even if it costs you your reputation?
?
Al-Badawi never married and was absorbed into eternity. Do you fear that your attachments to family and friends are preventing you from reaching that same absorption? What is one attachment you know you need to loosen but have not?

Life of Imam al-Sawi

His Asceticism and the Divine Call to Tanta
Description of al-Badawi's extreme asceticism and his divinely-guided journey to Egypt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extreme ascetic practices of Ahmad al-Badawi, the divine call that directed him to Tanta, his encounter with two great saints who offered him spiritual keys, and his reliance on Allah alone.

Core Idea
Al-Badawi's asceticism was so intense that he fasted forty days without eating, and he refused spiritual authority except from Allah.

This lesson delves into al-Badawi's remarkable ascetic feats—fasting for forty days without food or drink, staring at the sky—and his journey following a heavenly caller. It also recounts his encounter with al-Kilani and al-Rifa'i, where he famously refused their offer of keys, demonstrating his complete trust in Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the second paragraph
Read from 'He would remain forty days...' up to '...entered Egypt in the year 634 AH.' Focus on the ascetic practices and the journey.
Pay attention to the details of his fasting, sleeplessness, and the description of his eyes.
2
Analyze the divine call
The caller instructs him to go to the sunrise, then sunset, then to Tanta. This shows that his movements were divinely directed.
3
Understand the encounter with al-Kilani and al-Rifa'i
They offer him keys to various regions, but he refuses, saying he only takes the key from al-Fattah. This highlights his tawakkul (reliance on Allah).
This is a key moment showing his independence from human authority.

تراجم رجال التصوف
أبوه سنة سبع وعشرين وسنّ مئة، ودفن بالمعلا .
وعرف بالبدوي للزومه اللثام، ولبس لثامين فلم يفارقهما، ولم يتزوّج قط، واشتهر بالعطاب؛ لكثرة عطبه من يؤذيه، ثمَّ لزم الصمت، فكان لا يتكلم إلا بإشارة، وتوله، ثم حصلت له جمعيَّة على الحقِّ فاستغرق إلى الأبد، وكان عظيم الفتوة.
قال المتبولي : قال لي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «ما في أولياء مـصـر بـعـد بن إدريس أكبر فتوة منه، ثمَّ نفيسة، ثمَّ شرف الدين الكردي، ثمَّ محمد المنوفي» انتهى .
وكان يمكث أربعين يوماً لا يأكل ولا يشرب ولا ينام وأكثر أوقاته شاخص ببصره نحو السَّماء وعيناه كالجمرتين ، ثم يسمع هاتفاً يقول ثلاثاً : قم واطلب مطلع الشمس، فإذا وصلته فاطلب مغربها، وسر إلى طندتا فيها مقامك أيُّها الفتى فسار إلى العراق فتلقاه العارفان الكيلاني والرفاعي فقالا يا أحمد؛ مفاتيح العراق والهند واليمن، والمشرق والمغرب بيدينا، فاختر أيُّها شئت، فقال: لا آخذ المفتاح إلا من يد الفتّاح. ثم رحل إلى مصر فتلقاه الظاهر بيبرس بعسكره، وأكرمه وعظمه، فدخلها سنة أربع وثلاثين وست مئة .
فأقام بطندتا على سطح دار لا يفارقه ليلاً ولا نهاراً اثنتي عشرة سنة، وإذا عرض له الحال صاح صياحاً عظيماً .
.
وتبعه جمع ؛ منهم عبد العال وعبد المجيد.
ولما دخل طندتا كان بها جمع من الأولياء؛ فمنهم من خرج منها هيبة له ؛ كالشَّيخ حسن الإخناني، فسكن إخنان حتَّى مات، وضريحه بها ظاهر يزار .
ومنهم من مكث ؛ كالشَّيخ سالم المغربي ، وسالَمَ الشَّيخ البدوي، فأقره على حاله حتّى مات بطندتا، وقبره بها مشهور.
ومنهم من أنكر عليه ؛ كصاحب الإيوان العظيم بطندتا المسمى بوجه القمر كان وليّاً كبيراً فثار به الحسد فسلبه ، ومحله الآن بطندتا مأوى الكلاب وليس فيه رائحة صلاح ولا مدد.
وكان الله إذا لبس ثوباً أو عمامة لا يخلعها لا لغسل ولا غيره حتّى تبلى فتبدل، وإذا أمر أحداً من أصحابه بالإقامة في مكان لا يمكنه مخالفته .
وكان يعرف من هو من أولاده بالكشف، ولا يقبل إلَّا من علمه منهم . وكان لا يكشف اللثام عن وجهه، فقال له عبد المجيد : أرني وجهك قال : كل نظرة برجل قال أرنيه فكشف، فمات حالاً. وله كرامات شهيرة جداً منها : قصَّة المرأة التي أسر ولدها الإفرنج، فلاذت به فأحضره في قيوده.
ومرَّ به رجل يحمل قربة لبن فأشار بإصبعه إليها، فانقدت، فخرج
Biographies of the men of Sufism. His father was born in the year twenty-seven and one hundred [AH], and was buried in al-Ma'la. He was known as al-Badawi for his constant wearing of the litham [face veil]; he wore two lithams and never removed them, and he never married at all. He was famous as al-'Attab [the reproacher] because of the great destruction [that befell] whoever harmed him. Then he adhered to silence, and he would not speak except by gesture, and he was devoted. Then a spiritual gathering upon the truth came to him, so he was absorbed into eternity. He had great chivalry. Al-Mutawalli said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said to me: 'Among the saints of Egypt after Ibn Idris, none has greater chivalry than him, then Nafisa, then Sharaf al-Din al-Kurdi, then Muhammad al-Manufi.' End. He would remain forty days without eating, drinking, or sleeping, and most of his time he would stare at the sky with eyes like two embers. Then he would hear a caller saying three times: 'Arise and seek the rising of the sun; when you reach it, seek its setting; and travel to Tanta, for there is your station, O youth.' So he traveled to Iraq, and the two gnostics al-Kilani and al-Rifa'i met him and said: 'O Ahmad, the keys of Iraq, India, Yemen, the east and the west are in our hands; choose whichever you wish.' He said: 'I will not take the key except from the hand of the Opener [al-Fattah].' Then he journeyed to Egypt, and al-Zahir Baybars met him with his army and honored and venerated him. He entered it in the year thirty-four and six hundred [AH]. He resided in Tanta on the roof of a house, never leaving it night or day for twelve years. When a state [of spiritual ecstasy] came over him, he would scream a great scream. A group followed him, among them 'Abd al-'Al and 'Abd al-Majid. When he entered Tanta, there was a group of saints there. Among them were those who left out of awe of him, like Shaykh Hasan al-Ikhnani; he settled in Ikhna until he died, and his tomb there is visible and visited. Among them were those who stayed, like Shaykh Salim al-Maghribi; he made peace with Shaykh al-Badawi, who allowed him to remain as he was until he died in Tanta, and his grave there is well-known. Among them were those who opposed him, like the owner of the great iwan [hall] in Tanta called Wajh al-Qamar; he was a great saint, but envy rose in him and stripped him [of his spiritual state]; his place in Tanta is now a shelter for dogs, and there is in it no trace of righteousness or spiritual support. And [al-Badawi] would, when he wore a garment or a turban, not remove it—neither for washing nor for anything else—until it wore out, then he would replace it. And when he commanded one of his companions to stay in a place, it was impossible for him to disobey. And he would know who among his descendants were [truly his] through spiritual unveiling, and he would accept only those he knew to be [genuine]. And he would not remove the litham from his face. 'Abd al-Majid said to him: 'Show me your face.' He said: 'Every glance is a [fatal] blow.' 'Abd al-Majid said: 'Show me.' So he uncovered [his face], and [Abd al-Majid] died instantly. He had very famous miracles, among them: the story of the woman whose son was captured by the Franks; she sought his refuge, and he brought him in his chains. And a man passed by him carrying a waterskin of milk; he pointed his finger at it, and it split, and [the milk] came out.
Source pages p. 454

This passage is a biographical sketch of the Sufi saint Ahmad al-Badawi. It begins by stating his father's death year and burial place, then explains his nickname 'al-Badawi' from his constant wearing of the face veil (litham). It notes that he never married. How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Badawi fasted forty days without food or drink. What is the longest you have gone without something you crave for the sake of Allah? Does your life reflect any real hunger for God, or are you spiritually satisfied with comfort?
?
When offered spiritual authority or status, al-Badawi said, 'I will not take the key except from the hand of al-Fattah.' In what areas of your life (teaching, leadership, influence) do you seek validation from people rather than from Allah alone? What would it cost you to refuse every key except His?
?
The divine caller directed al-Badawi to a specific place. If Allah were to send you a clear instruction today, would you obey immediately, or would you hesitate with excuses? What is holding you back from complete surrender to His guidance?

His Sojourn in Tanta and Interactions with Other Saints
Al-Badawi's seclusion in Tanta and the varied responses of local saints.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Badawi settled in Tanta for twelve years on a rooftop, his spiritual ecstasies, and the varied reactions of the local saints—some leaving out of awe, some staying in peace, and some opposing him out of envy.

Core Idea
Al-Badawi's presence in Tanta caused a division among local saints, showcasing the power of his spiritual station.

This lesson details al-Badawi's long seclusion on a rooftop in Tanta, his occasional fits of spiritual ecstasy, and the arrival of disciples. It then describes how the saintly community in Tanta reacted: some left out of reverence, some remained in harmony, and one great saint fell from grace due to envy. This illustrates the transformative impact of a true saint.

Guided Path
1
Read about his stay in Tanta
Read from 'He resided in Tanta...' up to '...and his grave there is well-known.' Focus on the twelve years on the roof and his screaming.
Notice the exact duration and location.
2
Identify the three reactions of other saints
The passage lists three categories: those who left (like al-Ikhnani), those who stayed (like Salim al-Maghribi), and those who opposed (like Wajh al-Qamar).
Consider why each group reacted differently.
3
Reflect on the fate of the envious saint
Wajh al-Qamar's envy caused his spiritual status to be stripped. This is a moral lesson about the danger of envy.

The author then quotes al-Mutawalli, who reports a hadith from the Prophet praising al-Badawi's chivalry (futuwwa) as the greatest among Egyptian saints after Ibn Idris, followed by Nafisa and others. He hears a caller directing him to travel to Tanta, so he goes to Iraq, where the saints al-Kilani and al-Rifa'i offer him keys to various regions, but he refuses, relying solely on Allah. He then goes to Egypt, meets Sultan al-Zahir Baybars, and enters Egypt in 634 AH. He settles in Tanta on a rooftop for twelve years, sometimes screaming in spiritual ecstasy. The passage then describes the reactions of other saints to his arrival: some left out of awe, some stayed in peace, and some opposed him out of envy, losing their spiritual state. The author notes that al-Badawi never changed his clothes until they wore out. His authority over his companions was absolute. He used spiritual unveiling to know his true descendants. When 'Abd al-Majid insisted on seeing his face, al-Badawi warned him, but upon seeing it, 'Abd al-Majid died. Finally, two miracles are mentioned: recovering a captured boy from the Franks and a waterskin splitting at a gesture.

Checkpoint

A) He also became a great saint.

Key Takeaway
The varied reactions of local saints to al-Badawi show that encountering a great saint can either inspire awe, peaceful coexistence, or destructive envy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage shows that even a great saint like Wajh al-Qamar was stripped of his spiritual state because of envy. Reflect on your own heart: is there anyone you envy for their piety, knowledge, or spiritual gifts? What steps will you take today to uproot that envy before it destroys what you have?
?
Al-Badawi's presence caused some saints to leave out of awe and some to stay in peace. When you encounter someone more spiritually advanced, what is your immediate inner reaction? Do you feel threatened, defensive, or humbled? How can you cultivate the humility of Shaykh Salim al-Maghribi?
?
The fate of Wajh al-Qamar is a warning that spiritual rank does not protect against the consequences of envy. If you have been given some spiritual gift, are you guarding it with humility and gratitude, or are you at risk of losing it by looking down on others or feeling threatened by them?

His Spiritual Powers and Miracles
Al-Badawi's personal habits, his ability to know descendants by unveiling, the fatal face unveiling incident, and two miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two aspects of al-Badawi's spiritual authority: his ability to know his true descendants through unveiling and his refusal to show his face, as well as two of his famous miraculous deeds.

Core Idea
Al-Badawi's spiritual unveiling and miracles demonstrate his intimate connection with Allah and the intensity of his spiritual station.

This lesson focuses on al-Badawi's extraordinary spiritual powers: he could identify his genuine spiritual descendants through inner knowledge, and when a companion insisted on seeing his unveiled face, the result was fatal. The lesson also recounts two well-known miracles: recovering a boy captured by the Franks and splitting a waterskin with a gesture.

Guided Path
1
Read about his habit of not removing clothes and his authority
Read from 'And [al-Badawi] would, when he wore a garment...' up to '...died instantly.' This covers his personal habits and the face incident.
Note his absolute authority over companions.
2
Understand the significance of the face unveiling
Al-Badawi warns that seeing his face is lethal. When 'Abd al-Majid insists, he uncovers and the man dies. This shows the overwhelming spiritual power of a saint.
This demonstrates the difference between ordinary believers and the elect.
3
Read the miracles
Read from 'He had very famous miracles...' to the end. The two miracles involve recovering a captive and splitting a waterskin.
These confirm his saintly status and power.
