تراجم رجال التصوف
أبوه سنة سبع وعشرين وسنّ مئة، ودفن بالمعلا .
وعرف بالبدوي للزومه اللثام، ولبس لثامين فلم يفارقهما، ولم يتزوّج قط، واشتهر بالعطاب؛ لكثرة عطبه من يؤذيه، ثمَّ لزم الصمت، فكان لا يتكلم إلا بإشارة، وتوله، ثم حصلت له جمعيَّة على الحقِّ فاستغرق إلى الأبد، وكان عظيم الفتوة.
قال المتبولي : قال لي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «ما في أولياء مـصـر بـعـد بن إدريس أكبر فتوة منه، ثمَّ نفيسة، ثمَّ شرف الدين الكردي، ثمَّ محمد المنوفي» انتهى .
وكان يمكث أربعين يوماً لا يأكل ولا يشرب ولا ينام وأكثر أوقاته شاخص ببصره نحو السَّماء وعيناه كالجمرتين ، ثم يسمع هاتفاً يقول ثلاثاً : قم واطلب مطلع الشمس، فإذا وصلته فاطلب مغربها، وسر إلى طندتا فيها مقامك أيُّها الفتى فسار إلى العراق فتلقاه العارفان الكيلاني والرفاعي فقالا يا أحمد؛ مفاتيح العراق والهند واليمن، والمشرق والمغرب بيدينا، فاختر أيُّها شئت، فقال: لا آخذ المفتاح إلا من يد الفتّاح. ثم رحل إلى مصر فتلقاه الظاهر بيبرس بعسكره، وأكرمه وعظمه، فدخلها سنة أربع وثلاثين وست مئة .
فأقام بطندتا على سطح دار لا يفارقه ليلاً ولا نهاراً اثنتي عشرة سنة، وإذا عرض له الحال صاح صياحاً عظيماً .
.
وتبعه جمع ؛ منهم عبد العال وعبد المجيد.
ولما دخل طندتا كان بها جمع من الأولياء؛ فمنهم من خرج منها هيبة له ؛ كالشَّيخ حسن الإخناني، فسكن إخنان حتَّى مات، وضريحه بها ظاهر يزار .
ومنهم من مكث ؛ كالشَّيخ سالم المغربي ، وسالَمَ الشَّيخ البدوي، فأقره على حاله حتّى مات بطندتا، وقبره بها مشهور.
ومنهم من أنكر عليه ؛ كصاحب الإيوان العظيم بطندتا المسمى بوجه القمر كان وليّاً كبيراً فثار به الحسد فسلبه ، ومحله الآن بطندتا مأوى الكلاب وليس فيه رائحة صلاح ولا مدد.
وكان الله إذا لبس ثوباً أو عمامة لا يخلعها لا لغسل ولا غيره حتّى تبلى فتبدل، وإذا أمر أحداً من أصحابه بالإقامة في مكان لا يمكنه مخالفته .
وكان يعرف من هو من أولاده بالكشف، ولا يقبل إلَّا من علمه منهم . وكان لا يكشف اللثام عن وجهه، فقال له عبد المجيد : أرني وجهك قال : كل نظرة برجل قال أرنيه فكشف، فمات حالاً. وله كرامات شهيرة جداً منها : قصَّة المرأة التي أسر ولدها الإفرنج، فلاذت به فأحضره في قيوده.
ومرَّ به رجل يحمل قربة لبن فأشار بإصبعه إليها، فانقدت، فخرج
Biographies of the men of Sufism. His father was born in the year twenty-seven and one hundred [AH], and was buried in al-Ma'la. He was known as al-Badawi for his constant wearing of the litham [face veil]; he wore two lithams and never removed them, and he never married at all. He was famous as al-'Attab [the reproacher] because of the great destruction [that befell] whoever harmed him. Then he adhered to silence, and he would not speak except by gesture, and he was devoted. Then a spiritual gathering upon the truth came to him, so he was absorbed into eternity. He had great chivalry. Al-Mutawalli said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said to me: 'Among the saints of Egypt after Ibn Idris, none has greater chivalry than him, then Nafisa, then Sharaf al-Din al-Kurdi, then Muhammad al-Manufi.' End. He would remain forty days without eating, drinking, or sleeping, and most of his time he would stare at the sky with eyes like two embers. Then he would hear a caller saying three times: 'Arise and seek the rising of the sun; when you reach it, seek its setting; and travel to Tanta, for there is your station, O youth.' So he traveled to Iraq, and the two gnostics al-Kilani and al-Rifa'i met him and said: 'O Ahmad, the keys of Iraq, India, Yemen, the east and the west are in our hands; choose whichever you wish.' He said: 'I will not take the key except from the hand of the Opener [al-Fattah].' Then he journeyed to Egypt, and al-Zahir Baybars met him with his army and honored and venerated him. He entered it in the year thirty-four and six hundred [AH]. He resided in Tanta on the roof of a house, never leaving it night or day for twelve years. When a state [of spiritual ecstasy] came over him, he would scream a great scream. A group followed him, among them 'Abd al-'Al and 'Abd al-Majid. When he entered Tanta, there was a group of saints there. Among them were those who left out of awe of him, like Shaykh Hasan al-Ikhnani; he settled in Ikhna until he died, and his tomb there is visible and visited. Among them were those who stayed, like Shaykh Salim al-Maghribi; he made peace with Shaykh al-Badawi, who allowed him to remain as he was until he died in Tanta, and his grave there is well-known. Among them were those who opposed him, like the owner of the great iwan [hall] in Tanta called Wajh al-Qamar; he was a great saint, but envy rose in him and stripped him [of his spiritual state]; his place in Tanta is now a shelter for dogs, and there is in it no trace of righteousness or spiritual support. And [al-Badawi] would, when he wore a garment or a turban, not remove it—neither for washing nor for anything else—until it wore out, then he would replace it. And when he commanded one of his companions to stay in a place, it was impossible for him to disobey. And he would know who among his descendants were [truly his] through spiritual unveiling, and he would accept only those he knew to be [genuine]. And he would not remove the litham from his face. 'Abd al-Majid said to him: 'Show me your face.' He said: 'Every glance is a [fatal] blow.' 'Abd al-Majid said: 'Show me.' So he uncovered [his face], and [Abd al-Majid] died instantly. He had very famous miracles, among them: the story of the woman whose son was captured by the Franks; she sought his refuge, and he brought him in his chains. And a man passed by him carrying a waterskin of milk; he pointed his finger at it, and it split, and [the milk] came out.
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of the Sufi saint Ahmad al-Badawi. It begins by stating his father's death year and burial place, then explains his nickname 'al-Badawi' from his constant wearing of the face veil (litham). It notes that he never married. He was known as al-'Attab because harm would befall those who harmed him. He then adopted silence, communicating only by gesture. The phrase 'tawalla' (devotion) indicates his complete turning to God. He attained a spiritual state of absorption. The author then quotes al-Mutawalli, who reports a hadith from the Prophet praising al-Badawi's chivalry (futuwwa) as the greatest among Egyptian saints after Ibn Idris, followed by Nafisa and others. Next, al-Badawi's extraordinary asceticism is described: forty-day fasts without food, drink, or sleep, staring at the sky. He hears a caller directing him to travel to Tanta, so he goes to Iraq, where the saints al-Kilani and al-Rifa'i offer him keys to various regions, but he refuses, relying solely on Allah. He then goes to Egypt, meets Sultan al-Zahir Baybars, and enters Egypt in 634 AH. He settles in Tanta on a rooftop for twelve years, sometimes screaming in spiritual ecstasy. The passage then describes the reactions of other saints to his arrival: some left out of awe, some stayed in peace, and some opposed him out of envy, losing their spiritual state. The author notes that al-Badawi never changed his clothes until they wore out. His authority over his companions was absolute. He used spiritual unveiling to know his true descendants. When 'Abd al-Majid insisted on seeing his face, al-Badawi warned him, but upon seeing it, 'Abd al-Majid died. Finally, two miracles are mentioned: recovering a captured boy from the Franks and a waterskin splitting at a gesture.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that miracles prove sainthood independently of divine will.
Correction: Miracles are granted by Allah to honor His saints and are not performed by their own power.

Reactions of the Saints to al-Badawi's Arrival in Tantā
Describes three groups of saints' reactions to al-Badawi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the diverse reactions of saints to al-Badawi's arrival and the spiritual lesson that opposing a true saint can lead to loss of blessings.

Core Idea
Envy and opposition to true saints can strip one of spiritual rank.

When the great saint Ahmad al-Badawi entered Tantā, the resident saints reacted in different ways. This passage from the Hashiyah captures three distinct responses: some left out of awe, some stayed in peace, and one objected out of jealousy—with dire consequences. The text serves as a powerful reminder of the adab (etiquette) due to Allah's friends.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three reactions
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the three categories of saints: those who left, those who stayed, and those who objected.

Consider the story of the saint called Wajh al-Qamar whose jealousy stripped him of his rank, turning his place into a shelter for dogs.
This is a stark warning against envy.
3
Consider the lesson about respecting saints
Think about the importance of honoring true saints and avoiding any opposition to them, as it can lead to spiritual loss.
The passage teaches that true saints are recognized and respected by other saints.

ولما دخل طندتا كان بها جمع من الأولياء؛ فمنهم من خرج منها هيبة له ؛ كالشَّيخ حسن الإخناني، فسكن إخنان حتَّى مات، وضريحه بها ظاهر يزار . ومنهم من مكث ؛ كالشَّيخ سالم المغربي ، وسالَمَ الشَّيخ البدوي، فأقره على حاله حتّى مات بطندتا، وقبره بها مشهور. ومنهم من أنكر عليه ؛ كصاحب الإيوان العظيم بطندتا المسمى بوجه القمر كان وليّاً كبيراً فثار به الحسد فسلبه ، ومحله الآن بطندتا مأوى الكلاب وليس فيه رائحة صلاح ولا مدد.
When he entered Tantā, there was a group of saints there. Among them were those who stayed, like Sheikh Salim al-Maghribi, who made peace with Sheikh al-Badawi, so he left him as he was until he died in Tantā, and his grave there is famous. Commentary
This passage narrates the diverse reactions of saints when al-Badawi entered Tantā. It describes three groups: those who left out of respect, those who stayed and made peace, and one who objected and consequently lost his station. The author emphasizes the consequences of opposing a true saint.

Al-Badawi's Ascetic Habits and Spiritual Authority
Describes al-Badawi's ascetic habits and the fatal incident of his face.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Badawi's personal ascetic practices and how he exercised spiritual authority through kashf and the power of his hidden face.

Core Idea
A saint's discipline reveals divine favor—al-Badawi's habits were signs of his closeness to Allah.

This passage from al-Sawi's commentary describes the remarkable personal habits of the great saint Ahmad al-Badawi. It shows his detachment from worldly comforts, his unquestioned authority over his followers, and his ability to know his true spiritual children. The incident with 'Abd al-Majid demonstrates the dangerous power of his hidden face.

Guided Path
1

Understand his authority

3

He knew his true children through spiritual unveiling, accepting only those he recognized.
4
Reflect on the face incident
When 'Abd al-Majid insisted on seeing his face, al-Badawi warned 'Every look is a man'—yet the man died upon uncovering.
This shows the overwhelming baraka of the saint's countenance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكان الله إذا لبس ثوباً أو عمامة لا يخلعها لا لغسل ولا غيره حتّى تبلى فتبدل، وإذا أمر أحداً من أصحابه بالإقامة في مكان لا يمكنه مخالفته . وكان يعرف من هو من أولاده بالكشف، ولا يقبل إلَّا من علمه منهم . وكان لا يكشف اللثام عن وجهه، فقال له عبد المجيد : أرني وجهك قال : كل نظرة برجل قال أرنيه فكشف، فمات حالاً. وله كرامات شهيرة جداً منها : قصَّة المرأة التي أسر ولدها الإفرنج، فلاذت به فأحضره في قيوده. ومرَّ به رجل يحمل قربة لبن فأشار بإصبعه إليها، فانقدت، فخرج منها حيَّة انتفخت .
He used to, when he wore a garment or a turban, not take it off neither for washing nor for anything else until it wore out, then he would change it. When he ordered one of his companions to stay in a place, he could not disobey him. He used to know who among his children were his through kashf (unveiling), and he would only accept those he knew of them. He would not uncover his veil from his face. So 'Abd al-Majid said to him: 'Show me your face.' He said: 'Every look is a man.' He said: 'Show me.' So he uncovered, and he died instantly. He had very famous miracles, among them: the story of the woman whose son was captured by the Franks; she sought refuge with him, and he brought him in his chains. And a man passed by him carrying a water-skin of milk; he pointed his finger at it, it split, and a snake that had swollen came out of it.
Source pages p. 455

Commentary

Then it mentions two miracles: restoring a captive son and revealing a snake hidden in a water-skin, demonstrating his baraka.

Al-Badawi's Famous Miracles
Relates two famous miracles of al-Badawi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two major miracles of al-Badawi that demonstrate his saintly power and divine support.

Core Idea
Miracles confirm the saint's rank—al-Badawi's miracles show his ability to intervene in extraordinary ways.

After describing his personal habits, the passage turns to al-Badawi's well-known karamat. Two specific miracles are mentioned: the rescue of a captive son from the Franks and the exposure of a snake hidden in a water-skin. These events confirm his baraka and his role as a wali.

Read the second miracle

3

Source Text

وكان الله إذا لبس ثوباً أو عمامة لا يخلعها لا لغسل ولا غيره حتّى تبلى فتبدل، وإذا أمر أحداً من أصحابه بالإقامة في مكان لا يمكنه مخالفته . وكان يعرف من هو من أولاده بالكشف، ولا يقبل إلَّا من علمه منهم . وكان لا يكشف اللثام عن وجهه، فقال له عبد المجيد : أرني وجهك قال : كل نظرة برجل قال أرنيه فكشف، فمات حالاً. وله كرامات شهيرة جداً منها : قصَّة المرأة التي أسر ولدها الإفرنج، فلاذت به فأحضره في قيوده. ومرَّ به رجل يحمل قربة لبن فأشار بإصبعه إليها، فانقدت، فخرج منها حيَّة انتفخت .
He used to, when he wore a garment or a turban, not take it off neither for washing nor for anything else until it wore out, then he would change it. When he ordered one of his companions to stay in a place, he could not disobey him. He used to know who among his children were his through kashf (unveiling), and he would only accept those he knew of them. He would not uncover his veil from his face. Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage details al-Badawi's ascetic habits, his authority over his companions, his ability to know his true spiritual children through kashf, and his refusal to show his face until one who insisted died instantly. Then it mentions two miracles: restoring a captive son and revealing a snake hidden in a water-skin, demonstrating his baraka.

Key Terms
كرامات
البدوي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think these miracles are magic or deceptive tricks.
Correction: In Islamic theology, such karamat are real supernatural events granted by Allah to His saints as a sign of their rank and to benefit others.

Checkpoint
What was inside the water-skin that al-Badawi split?
A) Milk
B) Water
C) A snake
D) Blood

Key Takeaway
Al-Badawi's miracles, like rescuing a captive and revealing a hidden snake, confirm his sainthood and the power of his baraka.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The woman sought refuge with al-Badawi and her son was returned. When you face a crisis, do you turn to the awliya with full trust, or do you rely on your own efforts? What one step can you take today to strengthen your connection to a saint you respect?
?
The man unknowingly carried a deadly snake in his waterskin. Al-Badawi revealed it and saved him. What hidden dangers—spiritual or worldly—might be lurking in your own life? Will you ask a true wali to expose them before it is too late?
?
Al-Badawi's miracles show his power over matter. Do you believe that Allah can grant such abilities to His beloved servants in your own time? If not, what is holding you back from trusting in the ongoing baraka of the awliya?

Life of Imam al-Sawi
beginner
4 min
Ibn al-Laban's Loss and Restoration
Punishment and restoration of Ibn al-Laban after objecting to al-Badawi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how objecting to a saint can lead to loss of knowledge and how intercession can restore it.

Core Idea
Opposing saints can cause loss of blessings; sincere repentance and intercession can bring restoration.

This story from the biography of al-Badawi shows the severe consequences of criticizing a saint. Ibn al-Laban, a scholar, lost his Quranic knowledge after objecting to al-Badawi. Only after seeking help from saints did he regain it, illustrating the saint's spiritual authority and the power of intercession.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the sequence: objection, punishment, plea, intercession, restoration.
2
Identify the cause and effect
Identify what Ibn al-Laban did (objected) and what he lost (Quran and knowledge). Then see how he sought help and what happened.
3
Reflect on the lesson
Consider why the author includes this story. What does it teach about the status of saints and the consequences of opposing them?
The story ends with restoration, showing that repentance and intercession can reverse punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأنكر عليه ابن اللبان [ووقع فيه]، فسلب القرآن والعلم، فصار يستغيث بالأولياء حتّى أغاثه ياقوت العرشي فشفع له، فردَّ ذلك عليه. وأنكر عليه الشَّيخ خليفة الأبياري، وحطّ على من يحضر مولده، فابتلى بحيَّة قرصت فمه ولسانه فمات. واجتمع به ابن دقيق العيد، فقال له : إنَّك لا تصلى ما هذا سنن الصَّالحين، فقال: اسكت وإلَّا طيَّرت دقيقك، ودفعه فإذا هو بجزيرة متّسعة جداً، فضاق ذرعه حتّى كاد يهلك فرأى الخضر، فقال له : لا بأس عليك، إنَّ مثل البدوي لا يعترض عليه، اذهب إلى هذه القبة وقف ببابها ؛ فإنَّه سيأتيك العصر ليصلي بالنَّاس، فتعلَّق بأذياله لعلَّ أن يعفو عنك، ففعل، فدفعه فإذا هو ببابه .
Ibn al-Laban objected to him and spoke against him, so he was stripped of the Quran and knowledge. He began to cry out for help to the saints until Yāqūt al-‘Arshī came to his aid and interceded for him, and that was restored to him. And Sheikh Khalīfa al-Abyārī objected to him and disparaged those who attend his mawlid, so he was afflicted with a snake that bit his mouth and tongue, and he died. And Ibn Daqīq al-‘Īd met him and said to him: 'You do not pray; this is not the way of the righteous.' He said: 'Be silent, or I will scatter your flour.' And he pushed him, and suddenly he was on a vast island. His distress became great until he almost perished. Then he saw al-Khiḍr, who said to him: 'No harm upon you. Indeed, the likes of al-Badawi are not to be objected to. Go to this dome and stand at its door; he will come to pray with the people in the afternoon. So cling to his skirt that perhaps he will forgive you.' He did so, and he pushed him, and suddenly he was at his door.
Source pages p. 456

Commentary
This passage recounts three cases of people who criticized al-Badawi and the immediate divine retribution they faced. Ibn al-Laban lost his knowledge, Sheikh Khalifa was bitten by a snake and died, and Ibn Daqīq al-‘Īd was transported to an island and saved only by the intervention of al-Khiḍr and al-Badawi's forgiveness. The lesson is that true saints are under divine protection.

Key Terms
بدوي
اعتراض
كرامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Once a saint punishes someone, it is irreversible and final.
Correction: The story shows that punishment can be reversed through intercession and repentance, as Ibn al-Laban's knowledge was restored.

Checkpoint
What happened to Ibn al-Laban after he objected to al-Badawi?
A) He was bitten by a snake and died.
B) He lost his Quranic knowledge and learning.
C) He was transported to an island.
D) He became a follower of al-Badawi.

Key Takeaway
Objecting to a saint can lead to loss of blessings, but sincere repentance and seeking intercession can restore them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of a time you criticized or felt resentment toward a person of religious knowledge or piety, what blessings do you fear you may have lost because of it? Will you seek to repair that with repentance and by turning to the righteous?
?
If you lost something precious in your deen, like the sweetness of worship or knowledge, would you cry out to the awliya' for help, trusting that Allah can restore it through their intercession? What prevents you from doing so right now?

Sheikh Khalifa's Fatal Snakebite
Punishment of Sheikh Khalifa al-Abyārī for objecting to al-Badawi and disparaging his mawlid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that disparaging a saint and his followers can result in immediate and fatal divine punishment.

Core Idea
Insulting a saint's mawlid and followers leads to a terrible death.

This brief but powerful story illustrates the dire consequences of not only objecting to a saint but also criticizing those who celebrate his mawlid. Sheikh Khalifa al-Abyārī was punished with a snake that bit his mouth and tongue, causing his death. The story underscores the sanctity of the saint and his rituals.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the two actions: objecting to the saint and disparaging those who attend his mawlid.
2
Identify the punishment
The punishment is specific: a snake bit his mouth and tongue—the very organs used to speak against the saint.
3
Reflect on proportionality
Why was the punishment a snake biting the mouth and tongue? What does this teach about the seriousness of speaking against saints?
The punishment fits the crime: the mouth and tongue that spoke evil were afflicted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

So cling to his skirt that perhaps he will forgive you.' He did so, and he pushed him, and suddenly he was at his door.

This passage recounts three cases of people who criticized al-Badawi and the immediate divine retribution they faced. Ibn al-Laban lost his knowledge, Sheikh Khalifa was bitten by a snake and died, and Ibn Daqīq al-‘Īd was transported to an island and saved only by the intervention of al-Khiḍr and al-Badawi's forgiveness. Checkpoint
What happened to Sheikh Khalifa after he disparaged those who attend al-Badawi's mawlid?
A) He repented and was forgiven.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This story shows a man punished for his words against a saint's followers. Have you ever mocked or belittled someone for their devotion? Can you recall a specific incident? What would you do differently today?
?
If your own tongue were to be held accountable for every critical word you speak about others' worship, what would happen? Starting now, what specific habit can you adopt to guard your speech?
?
The snake bit the very organs of his sin: the mouth and tongue. Is there any part of your body you regularly use in disobeying Allah? What concrete step can you take to turn that limb into a means of obedience starting this week?
